The parks and recreation administration division shall oversee the daily operations of the parks, recreation and community affairs department and administer and evaluate departmental policies and procedures, and provide quality recreational programming, facilities and special events for the entire community. (2)	Mathis Auditorium. The Mathis Auditorium division shall provide and maintain meeting facilities, including a multipurpose room of 5,000 square feet provided in the community for banquets and meetings, and a 1,200-seat auditorium facility with stage support for community groups, shows and concerts promoted by outside organizations. (3)	Jaycee Park. The Jaycee Park division shall provide a facility for meetings, rentals for private functions, instructional classes and camps for the entire community. (4)	Parks. The parks division shall maintain parks and facilities in a safe, attractive and accessible condition, and develop new parks for public use and provide a variety of recreational opportunities. (5)	Therapeutics. The therapeutics division shall provide: a.	Therapeutic programs designed to meet social, recreational and educational needs of the mentally and physically disabled community in the city and county; b.	A quality social, recreational and educational program to the mentally and physically disabled adults and children; and c.	Quality summer programs for the special needs population.(6)	Aquatics. The aquatics division shall provide quality aquatic programming that will benefit the citizens of the city and county, and provide a quality aquatic facility that is operated in compliance with the state standards. A pool is operated at the Fry Street location, which meets state pool operating and safety standards with hired, professionally trained aquatic managers and certified lifeguards. Such location provides a variety of aquatics, including swimming lessons, free swimming, specialty classes and summer events. (7)	Instructional programming. The instructional programming division will provide quality programming for the residents of the city and county, to include a variety of instructional, educational and informative programs. (8)	Athletic manager/coordinator. The athletic manager/coordinator oversees the daily athletic operations that are used in adult programs, weekend tournaments and special athletic events, as well as coordinating the training and supervision of all athletic personnel. (9)	Pinevale. The Pinevale division's responsibilities shall be to meet the athletic, recreational and social needs of the Pinevale Youth Center participants, by providing a variety of youth-oriented programs through the Pinevale Youth Center. (10)	Youth sports division. The youth sports division provides a quality, economical and community-oriented recreational youth sports program for the city and county citizens, by providing seasonal leagues for boys and girls four to 18 years of age, including baseball, football, basketball and soccer for boys, and softball, soccer, basketball and cheerleading for girls. (11)	Adult athletics. The adult athletics division offers a variety of programs and events to both adult men and women, which events consist of softball, basketball, soccer, football and tennis. (12)	Hosted tournaments. The hosted tournaments division provides quality tournaments for the citizens of the city and county. Such division currently provides 12 quality softball invitational tournaments per year; four state parks and recreation association hosted tournaments per year; and four American Softball Association tournaments per year. (13)	Senior citizens. The senior citizens division shall establish quality programs for all senior citizens 55 years of age and older. Such division also provides facilities and programs for senior activities and instructional programming. A senior center is currently under construction, and the construction is funded jointly by the city and county. (14)	Special events. The special events division provides special events for the recreation of the county and city. (15)	After school program. The after school program division provides afternoon activities for elementary school age children in the community. (16)	Summer camp program. The summer camp program division provides an eight-week summer day camp for school age children in the city and county. Such division provides a quality eight-week camp program for an average of 30 children per site, per week. 
Sec. 2-317. - Capital improvements.     Unless otherwise agreed by separate written agreement, the county and cities agree and understand that the funding contemplated by the agreement as set forth in section 2-315 shall be for the annual operating budget of the county-wide recreational program. Any capital improvement or acquisitions of parks or other facilities for recreational purposes shall be at the expense of the individual government or by separate contract between the parties, or any combination thereof. 
Sec. 2-318. - Parks and recreation department.     The current and future employees of the city parks and recreation department and the current director shall continue to be considered employees of the city and subject to all of the benefits granted city employees and the personnel rules, regulations and procedures of the city, including its grievance procedure. Upon a vacancy in the office of director, the city and county will jointly conduct a solicitation phase for the hiring of a director. The city manager and county manager will jointly hire any new director. 
Sec. 2-319. - Director's duties.     The director shall be responsible for the general organization and staffing for the parks and recreation program, including, but not limited to, the following: (1)	Report to and be responsible to the city manager.(2)	Develop a plan for the parks and recreation program.(3)	Prepare an annual budget for the parks and recreation program. In the preparation of the budget, the director will work closely with the county manager, city manager and the parks and recreation board. The budget will be submitted on the format approved by the county finance department. (4)	Maintain complete and accurate records, under the supervision of the city's private sector certified public accountant, of all activities of the parks and recreation program and all receipts and disbursements of funds. A copy of such audit is to be furnished to the county each year. (5)	Oversee the execution of the parks and recreation program plan.(6)	Attend the monthly meeting of the advisory board and respond to their suggestions and inquiries. (7)	Make monthly reports to the advisory board, city manager and county manager, as they may require. (8)	Such other duties as may be prescribed by the city manager.
Secs. 2-320—2-330. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 4. - TREE COMMISSION 
Sec. 2-331. - Creation and purpose.     There is created a commission to be known and designated as the city tree commission for the purpose of regulating the planting, maintenance and removal of trees and shrubs in public places, providing for the pruning and removal of trees on private property which endanger public safety, and to generally improve the general welfare and health of the people of the city and the county. (Code 1976, § 2-8061; Ord. No. 84-25, § 1, 8-9-1984)
Sec. 2-332. - Members; terms; vacancies.     The tree commission shall consist of nine members as follows: Seven members shall be appointed by the mayor and council; the director of public works shall be an ex officio member, and the director of the department of leisure services shall be an ex officio member; an appointed member of the mayor and council shall serve as an ex officio member also. The seven members appointed by the mayor and council shall be citizens of the city, and the respective terms of the members shall begin as follows: (1)	One member for one year;(2)	Two members for three years; and(3)	Four members for four-year terms;and thereafter upon the expiration of such terms, successors shall be appointed for a term of four years by the mayor and council. Vacancies caused by death, resignation or otherwise shall be filled for the unexpired term by the mayor and council. (Code 1976, § 2-8062; Ord. No. 84-25, § 2, 8-9-1984; Ord. No. 86-22, 4-10-1986)
Sec. 2-333. - Powers and authority.     The tree commission shall have the power and authority to: (1)	Study and determine the problems and needs of the city for the planting of trees and shrubberies in public places. (2)	Recommend to the proper authorities and officials of the city the types and kinds of trees or shrubs to be planted upon the right-of-way of municipal streets, public parks and public facilities. (3)	Assist the city and parks and recreation department in a program to protect and maintain existing trees, shrubs and green areas on all city-owned property and public properties. (4)	Recommend to the mayor and council removal of any trees or shrubbery deemed to be hazardous to the public safety or public health. (5)	a.	Assist the proper officials and make available to the general public news and information regarding the selection, planting and maintenance of trees, shrubbery and other greenery within the corporate limits of the city; b.	Recommend from time to time as necessary ordinances and other programs that will be beneficial to protect and maintain existing trees, shrubs and green areas; and c.	Encourage the development of private property owners of landscaped areas with trees and shrubs. (Code 1976, § 2-8063; Ord. No. 84-25, § 3, 8-9-1984)
Sec. 2-334. - Officers and meetings.     Upon appointment of the initial tree commission by the mayor and council, the commission shall meet and elect one of its members as chairman and one of its members as secretary. The commission shall then provide for the rules and procedures for the holding of regular and special meetings of the commission as deemed advisable and necessary. (Code 1976, § 2-8064; Ord. No. 84-25, § 4, 8-9-1984)
Secs. 2-335—2-360. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 5. - PLANNING COMMISSION 
Sec. 2-361. - Creation of the Greater Lowndes Planning Commission.     There is established a Greater Lowndes Planning Commission to succeed to the general powers, duties and responsibilities of the former Greater Lowndes County Planning Commission, and as more fully set forth in this division. All acts, decisions, determinations and findings heretofore made by the abolished Greater Lowndes County Planning Commission are ratified and confirmed and shall remain in force and effect until changed. Any unfinished business of the abolished Greater Lowndes County Planning Commission, including any scheduled hearings or hearings in progress, shall be assumed, continued and carried out by the new commission. All 13 membership appointments of the abolished Greater Lowndes County Planning Commission shall continue uninterruptedly until the expiration date of their term as original members of the new commission. Future membership appointments and reappointments, including the addition of a 14th member representing the City of Dasher, shall continue as prescribed in section 2-362. (Ord. No. 96-56, § 2, 12-5-1996)
Sec. 2-362. - Membership.     The planning commission shall consist of 14 appointed members: five members appointed from the county commission, five from the mayor and council, two appointed by the mayor and council of the City of Hahira, one appointed by the mayor and council of the City of Lake Park, and one appointed by the mayor and council of the City of Dasher. All members shall be appointed for five-year terms and until their successors are appointed. (Ord. No. 96-56, § 3, 12-5-1996)
Sec. 2-363. - Compensation.     All members of the planning commission shall serve without compensation but shall be reimbursed for actual expenses incurred in connection with their official duties. (Ord. No. 96-56, § 4, 12-5-1996)
Sec. 2-364. - Organization, rules, staff and officers.     The planning commission shall elect from its members a chairman and a vice-chairman, each to serve for a term of one calendar year and until a successor is elected. The commission shall meet at least once each month at the call of the chairman and at such other times as the chairman or majority of commission members shall determine. The commission shall adopt rules and regulations for the conduct of its meetings and the transaction of its business, and shall keep records of its resolutions, motions, transactions, findings, determinations and recommendations. These records shall be public records. The commission may appoint such employees and staff as it deems necessary for its work, within the budget provided for its operation by the respective member governments, or other funds lawfully available to it. (Ord. No. 96-56, § 5, 12-5-1996)
Sec. 2-365. - Finances.     In the performance of its duties, the planning commission may cooperate with, contract with, and accept funds from federal, state, local, public or semi-public agencies, or private individuals or corporations, and may expend such funds and carry out cooperative undertakings and contracts with any of them within its lawful powers. The commission is authorized to make expenditures for the purchase of required equipment and supplies, all, with exception of gifts to the commission or contract receipts, to be within the amounts appropriated for the purpose by the member governments of the commission. Notwithstanding any other provisions of this division to the contrary, all checks or other orders of the commission for the withdrawal of money from banking institutions shall be signed in accordance with the commission's operating procedures as authorized by the member governments. (Ord. No. 96-56, § 6, 12-5-1996)
Sec. 2-366. - Powers, duties and responsibilities. (a)	It shall be the function and duty of the planning commission, subject to the direction and control of the respective member governments, to make surveys and studies of existing conditions and future developments and to prepare such plans for physical, social and economic growth as will best promote the public health, safety, morals, convenience, prosperity, general welfare, efficiency and economy in the development of the member governments. In particular, the commission shall have the power and duty, subject to the direction and control of the member governments, to: (1)	Prepare and maintain a local comprehensive plan for each of the member governments in accordance with state guidelines and regulations, and make recommendations on any amendments to such plan. (2)	Prepare and recommend to the member governments the adoption of amendments or revisions to local development regulations, including zoning ordinances and maps, subdivision regulations, special ordinances, and the like. (3)	Prepare and recommend to the member governments for the adoption of subdivision plats, or official maps, and amendments, showing the exact location of the boundary lines of existing, proposed, extended, widened, narrowed or closed streets, public open spaces, or public building sites. (b)	The commission shall have such additional duties and responsibilities and shall perform such additional functions and services as may be called for by the member governments. (Ord. No. 96-56, § 7, 12-5-1996)
Secs. 2-367—2-390. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 6. - HISTORIC PRESERVATION COMMISSION 
Sec. 2-391. - Creation and purpose.     There is created a commission to be known as the Valdosta Historic District Preservation Commission, which shall be part of the planning function of the city. (Code 1976, § 2-8070)
Sec. 2-392. - Members; terms; vacancies.     The historic preservation commission shall consist of seven members appointed by the mayor and council, who shall be residents of the city and who have demonstrated special interest, experience or education in history, architecture, or the preservation of historic resources. The term of office for each commission member shall be three years. On appointment of the first commission, two members shall be appointed for a term of three years, two members for a term of two years, and two members for a term of one year. All appointments thereafter shall be for a term of three years. In the event of a vacancy, the appointment shall be for the unexpired term in the same manner as the initial appointment. Members of the commission shall serve without compensation, although they may be reimbursed for expenses incurred. (Code 1976, § 2-8071; Ord. No. 85-5, 2-13-1985)
Sec. 2-393. - Powers.     The commission created in this division shall be authorized to: (1)	Prepare and maintain an inventory of all property within the city having the potential for designation as historic property. (2)	Recommend to the mayor and council specific places, districts, buildings, structures, objects or works of art to be designated by ordinance as historic properties or historic districts. (3)	Review applications for certificates of appropriateness, and grant or deny such applications in accordance with the provisions of this division. (4)	Recommend to the mayor and council that the designation of any place, district, site, building, structure, objects or works of art as an historic property or as an historic district or as part of an historic district be revoked or removed. (5)	Promote the acquisition by the city of facade easements and conservation easements in accordance with the provisions of the Facade and Conservation Easement Act of 1976 (O.C.G.A. § 44-10-1 et seq.). (6)	Conduct educational programs on historical properties located within the city and on general historic preservation activities. (7)	Make such investigations and studies on matters relating to historic preservation, including the consultation with historic preservation experts as the mayor and council or the commission itself may deem necessary or appropriate for the purposes of preserving historic resources. (8)	Seek out local, state, federal and private funds for historic preservation and make recommendations to the mayor and council concerning the most appropriate uses of any funds acquired. (9)	Submit to the historic preservation section of the department of natural resources a list of historic properties or historic districts designated and review and make comments to this agency concerning the nomination of properties within its jurisdiction to the National Register of Historic Places. (10)	Perform historic preservation activities as the official agency of the city historic preservation programs. (11)	Participate in private, state and federal historic preservation programs and with the consent of the mayor and council enter into agreements to do so. (Code 1976, § 2-8072)
Sec. 2-394. - Adoption of rules and standards.     The historic preservation commission shall adopt rules and standards for the transaction of its business and for consideration of application for designations and certificates of appropriateness, such as bylaws, removal of membership, provisions, and designated guidelines and criteria. The commission shall have the authority to adopt rules and standards without amendment to this division. (Code 1976, § 2-8073)
Sec. 2-395. - Officers and meetings; public records.     The historic preservation commission shall also provide for the time and place of its regular meetings and a method for calling of special meetings. The commission shall elect such officers as it deems appropriate from among its members. A quorum of the commission shall consist of a majority of the members. All meetings of the commission shall be public meetings, and a public record shall be kept of the commission's resolutions, proceedings and actions. (Code 1976, § 2-8074)
Sec. 2-396. - Conflict of interest.     At any time the historic preservation commission reviews a project or application in which a member of the commission has ownership or other vested interest, or that member is employed by a financial institution that may be considering financing of the project or application, that particular member shall be prohibited from voting on the particular project or application. (Code 1976, § 2-8075)
Sec. 2-397. - Designation of historic districts and properties; criteria for selection of historic districts; preliminary research by commission.     The historic preservation commission shall compile and collect information and conduct surveys of historic resources within the city. The commission shall present to the mayor and council recommendations for historic districts and properties. Prior to the commission's recommendations of an historic district or historic property to the mayor and council for designation, the commission shall prepare a report consisting of: (1)	A physical description of the property or district.(2)	A statement of historical, cultural, architectural and/or aesthetic significance of the property or district. (3)	A map showing district boundaries and classifications of individual properties in the districts, or showing boundaries of individual historic properties. (4)	A statement justifying district or individual property boundaries.(5)	Representative photographs of the district or properties.(Code 1976, § 2-8076)
Sec. 2-398. - Boundaries of an historic district.     Boundaries of an historic district shall be included in the separate ordinances designating such districts and shall be shown on the official zoning map of the city. (Code 1976, § 2-8077)
Secs. 2-399—2-420. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 7. - KEEP LOWNDES-VALDOSTA BEAUTIFUL 
Sec. 2-421. - Created.     A Keep Lowndes-Valdosta Beautiful (KLVB) Commission is created for the purpose of assisting the city and the county in establishing community-wide policies for the purpose of decreasing the amount of loose refuse in the city and county and for the purpose of promoting and establishing beautification programs for the city and county. (Ord. No. 97-12, § I, 4-10-1997)
Sec. 2-422. - Duties. (a)	The duties of the KLVB commission shall be to:(1)	Promote public interest in the general improvement of the environment of the city and the county; (2)	Initiate, plan, direct and coordinate education programs for litter control for the community on a sustainable basis; (3)	Implement and maintain the Keep America Beautiful System;(4)	Study, investigate and develop plans for improving the health, sanitation, safety and cleanliness of the city and the county by beautifying the streets, highways, alleys, river and stream banks, lots, yards and other similar places in the city and county; (5)	Aid in the prevention of fires, diseases and other casualties by the removal and elimination of trash and other debris from the streets, highways, alleys, lots, yards, plots and other similar places; (6)	Encourage the placing, planting and/or preservation of trees, flowers, plants, shrubbery and other objects or ornamentation in the city and county; and (7)	Advise and recommend plans and cooperate with other agencies for the beautification of the city and county. (b)	Nothing in this section shall be construed to abridge or change the powers and duties of other commissions, departments, boards and like agencies of the city or county, or the effect of other ordinances or resolutions regarding these matters adopted prior to April 10, 1997. (Ord. No. 97-12, § II, 4-10-1997)
Sec. 2-423. - Authority.     In order to perform its duties, the KLVB commission shall have the following authority: (1)	To adopt bylaws to facilitate the attainment of its purposes and functions.(2)	To initiate, plan, direct and coordinate community-wide efforts to achieve its goal.(3)	To solicit and accept donations and appropriations of money, services, products, property and facilities for expenditure and use by the commission for the fulfillment of commission purposes. (4)	To make recommendations to city and county governing bodies as well as to the private sector regarding measures which it deems necessary to accomplish its objectives. (Ord. No. 97-12, § III, 4-10-1997)
Sec. 2-424. - Membership.     The KLVB commission shall consist of not more than 12 voting members who shall be residents of the city and the county and who shall serve without remuneration. Four of the members shall be appointed by the city council, and four members shall be appointed by the board of commissioners of the county. Four members shall be appointed by the sitting KLVB commission. In addition to the appointed members of the commission, the solid waste manager for the county and the director of public works for the city shall serve as nonvoting ex officio members of the commission. (Ord. No. 97-12, § IV, 4-10-1997)
Sec. 2-425. - Terms of office of members.     The terms of office of the members of the KLVB commission shall generally be for three-year staggered terms, with approximately one-third of the membership being appointed every year. The terms of four of the 12 voting initial members selected will expire on June 30, 1998; terms of four of the initial members will expire on June 30, 1999; terms of the remaining four of the initial members will expire on June 30, 2000. Members may serve a maximum of two consecutive terms or six years. Members shall hold office until their successors have been appointed and qualified. The appropriate governing authority shall fill each vacancy from a list of names submitted by the commission. (Ord. No. 97-12, § V, 4-10-1997)
Sec. 2-426. - Officers.     The KLVB commission shall elect from its membership a chairman and such other officers as may be desired. Officers shall be elected on a fiscal year (July 1—June 30) basis for a term of one year but may be reelected for succeeding terms. (Ord. No. 97-12, § VI, 4-10-1997)
Sec. 2-427. - Disbursal of funds; records. (a)	The KLVB commission shall have the power to receive and disburse funds within the limitations of appropriations, gifts and grants which have been previously approved jointly by the city and the county, and in connection with projects or undertakings. Within the same limitation, the commission shall be empowered to contract with any private or public agency with the approval of the city and/or the county to the extent required for its proper operation and to create and contract with not-for-profit corporations. (b)	The commission shall keep such records as will enable it to make such reports and accountings as are requested by the city and/or the county, which shall be subject to verification and examination by auditors of the city and/or the county. (c)	Any project or undertaking begun by the commission shall be terminated at any time upon the decision of either the board of commissioners of the county or the city council that its continuance is not in the public interest. (Ord. No. 97-12, § VII, 4-10-1997)
Secs. 2-428—2-450. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 8. - AIRPORT AUTHORITY 
Sec. 2-451. - Created.     The Valdosta-Lowndes County Airport Authority is created and established effective May 1, 1987. (Ord. No. 87-8, § 1, 5-20-1987)
Sec. 2-452. - Assumption of airport control.     The airport authority shall assume the management and control of the Valdosta Municipal Airport effective May 1, 1987. (Ord. No. 87-8, § 2, 5-20-1987)
Secs. 2-453—2-470. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 9. - METROPOLOTIAN PLANNING ORGANIZATION 
Sec. 2-471. - Policy committee established.     The City of Valdosta and Lowndes County do hereby establish a Metropolitan Planning Organization (MPO) Policy Committee to ensure a continuing, cooperative, and comprehensive transportation planning process for the Valdosta/Lowndes MPO and that said policy committee be empowered to establish a technical coordinating committee, a citizens advisory committee and other ad hoc or advisory committees as required or deemed necessary. The MPO policy committee will: (1)	Be the forum for cooperative decision-making and shall consist of principal elected officials of the participating local general governments within the Valdosta/Lowndes County MPO area and appointed officials of designated agencies, which oversee or operate major transportation modes within the area. The MPO policy committee: a.	Reviews and approves all transportation study programs;b.	Ensures that the transportation program is current and responsive to laws, rules, regulations; c.	Designates and prioritizes transportation improvement projects recommended in the planning process; d.	Serves as liaison between the planning process and the governmental units and designates membership and operations of the technical coordinating committee, the citizens advisory committee and other ad hoc study committees. (2)	Consist of the following members:a.	Chairman, Lowndes County Board of Commissioners (or representative);b.	Mayor, City of Valdosta (or representative);c.	Annually rotating small city mayor (mayor or representative of Hahira, Lake Park, Remerton or Dasher); d.	Lowndes County Manager;e.	Valdosta Manager;f.	SGRDC executive director;g.	Georgia DOT Commissioner (or representative);h.	Nonvoting members:1.	Division administrator—Federal Highway Administration;2.	Regional administrator—Federal Transit Administration.(Res. No. 2003-16, 11-20-2003)
Secs. 2-472—2-475. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 10. - PUBLIC ART ADVISORY COMMITTEE 
Sec. 2-476. - Purpose of program.     It is the intent and purpose to create in the City of Valdosta a program to further the purchase and foster the appreciation of works of public art. Also to promote the creation of works of art and the purchase of same for the citizens and the City of Valdosta in order to promote the aesthetic value to the entire community and encourage the preservation and protection of works of public art and to encourage economic development. (Ord. No. 2010-9, § 1, 2-25-2010)
Sec. 2-477. - Public art advisory committee. (a)	There is hereby created a public art advisory committee to be appointed by Mayor and Council of the City of Valdosta to administer the public art program. (b)	The public art advisory committee shall consist of nine members. Five members appointed from the membership of the Lowndes-Valdosta Art Commission, including at least two professional artists and at least two members from the Board of Directors of the Lowndes-Valdosta Art Commission. One member from the general membership of the Lowndes-Valdosta Art Commission. Four members of the public art advisory committee shall be members of the community at large. (1)	The initial board shall be appointed by mayor and council as follows: One professional artist who is a member of the Lowndes-Valdosta Art Commission, one board member of Lowndes-Valdosta Art Commission and one member from the community at large for a term of three years; one professional artist who is a member of the Lowndes-Valdosta Art Commission, one member of the Board of Lowndes-Valdosta Art Commission and one member from the community at large for a term of two years; one member at large from the Lowndes-Valdosta Art Commission for a term of one year; two members from the community of the City of Valdosta for a term of one year. Thereafter members shall be appointed to three-year terms. (2)	Ex-officio members shall include a representative of the following departments to be determined by the city manager and the department head: Finance, planning and zoning, and public works. Ex-officio members shall also include the city manager and the mayor or the mayor's representative as appointed by the mayor. (3)	Five members shall reside, own property or work within the corporate limits of the City of Valdosta. The remaining four members shall be from the community at large. (Ord. No. 2010-9, § 1, 2-25-2010)
Sec. 2-478. - Powers and duties.     The public art advisory committee shall have the following powers and duties: (1)	The committee shall act as an advisory body to the mayor and the city council and as an advocate for public arts and aesthetics in all aspects of city life. It shall encourage, develop and support a variety of programs which reflect the cultural art needs and experience of all citizens and shall encourage participation by all citizens in the cultural art activities carried on in the city; (2)	Develop, maintain and update a public art master plan identifying locations for public artwork; (3)	Develop public art program guidelines and amendments thereto as deemed appropriate;(4)	Approve the location and installation of artwork based on public art program guidelines; and (5)	Request annual funding from various public, private, foundation and other potential sources to support the capital and operational needs of the public art program. (Ord. No. 2010-9, § 1, 2-25-2010)
Sec. 2-479. - Election of officers, quorum, bylaws, procedures of meetings.     Each year, the membership of the public art advisory committee shall meet as soon as practical after the effective date of this division and shall elect from among themselves a chairperson and vice-chairperson, each of whom shall continue as voting members. The chairperson shall preside over the meetings of the committee and the vice-chairperson shall preside in his or her absence. Such officer shall have such other powers, duties and responsibilities as are set out elsewhere herein. The committee shall also choose a secretary who may or may not be a member of the committee to keep minutes and records of the committee. Five members of the committee shall constitute a quorum. A majority of a quorum may exercise any and all powers of the committee. The committee may adopt its own bylaws, rules and procedures to govern internal workings in the conduct of its business. The committee shall meet at least quarterly and at such other times as it may deem necessary. (Ord. No. 2010-9, § 1, 2-25-2010)
Sec. 2-480. - Compensation of members.     The members shall receive no compensation but shall be reimbursed from the funds of the committee for reasonable and necessary expenses incurred in pursuing the business of the committee. (Ord. No. 2010-9, § 1, 2-25-2010)
Sec. 2-481. - Funding. (a)	There shall be created a public art fund administered by the public art advisory committee which shall consist of all contributions received from cash grants and donations to the program for public art projects from governmental or private resources, and all other funds allocated by the City of Valdosta through the budgetary process for the purchase and fostering of public art. (b)	The public art fund shall be used solely for expenses associated with the selection, commissioning, acquisition, transportation, maintenance, education promotion, administrative duties, removal and insurance of works of art. (Ord. No. 2010-9, § 1, 2-25-2010)
Sec. 2-482. - Ownership of artwork.     Unless otherwise expressly agreed in writing ownership and title of all art acquired through spending of funds in the public art fund shall be vested in the City of Valdosta. (Ord. No. 2010-9, § 1, 2-25-2010)
Sec. 2-483. - Program guidelines and master plan.     The public art advisory committee may adopt specific criteria for review of proposed permanent public art projects and guidelines therefore. (1)	The initial guidelines and criteria for review of proposed permanent public art projects shall be as follows: a.	Relevance of the work to the City of Valdosta, its values, culture and people;b.	Technical suitability of the work for outdoor display, including its maintenance and conservation requirements; and c.	Relationship of the work to the site, especially how it serves to activate or enhance the public space. (2)	In general, a proposed work of public art will not be accepted if it is not original sculpture or painting. If accepted artwork is a multiple, it will only be accepted if it is a limited edition. Generally reproductions; unlimited editions; decorative, ornamental and functional elements of architecture; directional elements, such as super graphics, signage and color-coding usually are not considered artwork unless done by an artist. a.	Acceptable media include:1.	Sculpture: in the round, bas-relief, mobile, fountain, kinetic, electronic;2.	Mosaic: ceramic, glass, metal, wood, mixed media;3.	Fountains or water elements;4.	Crafts: Clay fiber, textiles, wood, metal, plastics, stained glass;5.	Mixed media;6.	Earthworks and environmental artworks;7.	Decorative, ornamental or functional elements designed by an artist; and8.	Murals and paintings.b.	Unacceptable criteria: The artwork does not meet professional standards for public art due to one or more of the following: 1.	Faults of design or workmanship which will either pose a public safety hazard or diminish the value of the work. 2.	The possibility that the artwork is fraudulent or not authentic.3.	The artwork appears to be of inferior quality relative to the quality of other works in the city's collection. c.	The public art advisory committee will consider the following questions and criteria when conducting its review: 1.	Aesthetic quality and artistic merit;2.	Placement and sitting;3.	Fabrication, handling and installation;4.	Maintenance requirements;5.	Conservation and preservation;6.	Liability and safety; and7.	Community.(Ord. No. 2010-9, § 1, 2-25-2010)
Sec. 2-484. - Definitions.     As used in this division the following terms shall mean as follows:     Artists or professional artist. Practitioner in the visual arts, generally recognized by critics and peers as a professional of serious intent and ability. Indications of a person's status as a professional artist include, but are not limited to, income realized through the commission of artwork, frequent or consistent art exhibitions, placement of artwork in public institutions or museums, receipt of honors and awards, and training in the arts.     Art, artwork or works of art. Tangible creations by artists exhibiting the highest quality of skill and aesthetic principles and includes all forms of the visual arts conceived in any medium, material or combination thereof, including, but not limited to, paintings, sculptures, engravings, carvings, frescos, stained glass, mosaics, mobiles, tapestries, murals, photographs, video projections, digital images, bas-relief, high relief, fountains, kinetics, collages, drawings, monuments erected to commemorate a person or an event, functional furnishings, such as artist designed searing and pavers, architectural elements designed by an artist, and artist designed landforms or landscape elements. (1)	The following shall not be considered artwork or works of art for purposes of the program: a.	Reproductions or unlimited copies of original artwork.(Ord. No. 2010-9, § 1, 2-25-2010)
Secs. 2-485—2-490. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VI. - FINANCE[11] Footnotes: --- (11) --- Cross reference— Any ordinance or resolution promising or guaranteeing the payment of money for the city or authorizing the issuance of any bonds of the city or any evidence of the city's indebtedness saved from repeal, § 1-6(2); any contract or obligation assumed by the city saved from repeal, § 1-6(3); any appropriation ordinance saved from repeal, § 1-6(7); any ordinance providing for local improvements and assessing taxes therefor saved from repeal, § 1-6(9); any ordinance levying or imposing taxes not included in this Code saved from repeal, § 1-6(14); Sunset Hill Trust Fund, § 26-91 et seq.; taxation, ch. 90.State Law reference— Discretion of governing body as to management and disposition of property, O.C.G.A. § 36-30-2; grants of state funds to municipalities, O.C.G.A. § 36-40-1 et seq.; establishment of fiscal year required, O.C.G.A. § 36-81-3; accounting for public funds, O.C.G.A. § 45-8-1 et seq.
DIVISION 1. - GENERALLY 
Sec. 2-491. - Depository; withdrawal of funds.     All funds of the city shall be deposited with the depository designated by the mayor and council and shall be withdrawn from such depository only upon checks signed as authorized from time to time by resolution of the mayor and council. (Code 1976, § 2-5005; Ord. No. 97-21, 4-24-1997; Ord. No. 2009-29, 5-7-2009)
Sec. 2-492. - Bonds for public contractors.     No contract with the City of Valdosta for the doing of any public work in excess of $20,000 shall be valid for any purpose unless the contractor shall give: (1)	A performance bond with good and sufficient surety or sureties payable to, in favor of, and for the protection of the City of Valdosta. The performance bond shall be in an amount at least the total amount payable by the terms of the contract. (2)	A payment bond with good and sufficient surety or sureties payable to the City of Valdosta and for the use and protection of all subcontractors and for all persons supplying labor, materials, machinery and equipment in the prosecution of the work provided for in the contract. The payment bond shall be in the amount of at least a total amount payable by the terms of the contract. (Code 1976, § 2-5006; Ord. No. 88-35, 7-26-1988; Ord. No. 97-21, 4-24-1997; Ord. No. 2009-29, 5-7-2009) 
Secs. 2-493—2-510. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 2. - PURCHASING PROCEDURE[12] Footnotes: --- (12) --- Editor's note—Ord. No. 2009-29, adopted May 7, 2009, amended div. 2 in its entirety to read as herein set out. Former div. 2, §§ 2-511—2-514, pertained to similar subject matter and derived from Code 1976, §§ 2-5001—2-5004; Ord. No. 82-18, adopted Apr. 8, 1982; and Ord. No. 97-21, adopted Apr. 24, 1997.
Sec. 2-511. - Purchase orders required.     Purchases made by the city shall be made either by purchase order or procurement card. All purchase orders shall be signed by the city manager, deputy city manager of administration or other person designated by the city manager to act in the capacity when not utilizing the city procurement card. Other procurement information may be obtained by reading the City of Valdosta Purchasing Policy and Procedure Manual. The city will not be obligated to recognize claims for payment of materials, supplies and equipment issued without the authority of such purchase order or procurement card receipt. (Ord. No. 2009-29, 5-7-2009)
Sec. 2-512. - Purchases of $25,000.00 or more, specific pricing of construction projects for city departments, and information technology hardware and software. (a)	Except as provided for in subsection (b), purchase orders or procurement card transactions for amounts of $25,000.00 or more will be issued after approval of the mayor and council and after the receipt of sealed, competitive bids opened at a prior specified time by the city manager, deputy city manager of administration or another city employee designated by the city manager or mayor and council to act in this capacity in the presence of representatives of competing bidders, or in the event no bidders or representatives are present, at least two witnesses shall be present; provided, however, that competitive bids shall not be required if only one source of supply exist, an existing city annual contract, or an approved state or other governmental contract is in place for the desired product or service in which the contract pricing will be used. At least seven calendar days prior to the receipt of bids, except in the case of utmost urgency, a notice of the city's intent to receive bids shall be printed one time in a newspaper of general circulation in the city. (b)	Specific pricing of construction projects under $50,000.00. Purchase orders for amounts up to $50,000.00 will be issued only after approval of the city manager, deputy city manager of administration or any other city employee designated by the city manager or mayor and council and after the receipts of competitive pricing, by the requesting department from consultants and/or contractors for expedition including procurement of professional services and the award of construction contracts. Competitive prices will be independently verified by at least two individuals including the contract manager, purchasing agent or any other city employee designated by the city manager or mayor and council. (c)	The South Georgia RDC or Information Technology Manager with approval from the city manager or deputy city manager of administration will be responsible for procuring all information technology hardware and software utilizing the best source of supply available with regards to price, service and standardization. Purchase order amounts or procurement card transactions may exceed $25,000.00 and be exempt from mayor and council approval; however, orders will be issued only after approval of the city manager, deputy city manager of administration or any other city employee designated by the mayor and council. (Ord. No. 2009-29, 5-7-2009)
Sec. 2-513. - Purchases between $10,000.00 and $25,000.00.     Purchase orders or procurement card transactions for amounts in excess of $10,000.00 but less than $25,000.00 shall be issued only after the receipt of competitive prices in writing by mail, e-mail, facsimile or internet; provided, however, that competitive prices shall not be required if only one source of supply exist, an existing city annual contract, or an approved state or other governmental contract is in place for the desired product or service in which the contract pricing will be used. (Ord. No. 2009-29, 5-7-2009)
Sec. 2-514. - Purchases between $1,000.00 and $10,000.00.     Purchase orders or procurement card transactions for amounts in excess of $1,000.00 but less than $10,000.00 or less shall be issued to the vendor who quotes the best price or has provided similar products or service with an acceptable level of performance over the past year to the using department with prior approval from the city manager, deputy city manager of administration or another city employee designated by the city manager or mayor and council to act in this capacity. (Ord. No. 2009-29, 5-7-2009)
Sec. 2-515. - Purchases less than $1,000.00.     Purchase orders or procurement card transactions less than $1,000.00 may be made by any department that has funds available using their own discretion whereas quotes are not necessary but recommended. (Ord. No. 2009-29, 5-7-2009)
Secs. 2-516—2-540. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 3. - BUDGETS[13] Footnotes: --- (13) --- State Law reference— Appointment of budget officer, O.C.G.A. § 36-81-4; preparation of proposed budget, O.C.G.A. § 36-81-5; adoption of budget ordinance, O.C.G.A. § 36-81-6.
Sec. 2-541. - Completion of annual operating budget requests. (a)	Generally. The individual budget requests for the annual operating budget shall be completed in three separate steps or phases: (1)	A proposed work program for the ensuing budget year shall be determined;(2)	A basic budget consisting of the personal services, materials and supplies, capital outlay and other operating expenses necessary to complete the planned work program at the current level of operations shall be prepared; and (3)	Program change requests shall be prepared for all proposed new work programs or the expansion of current work programs. (b)	Work program. All departments and divisions shall plan their work program and estimate their work load for the ensuing budget year. An explanation of the work program and a tabulation of the work load data shall be submitted. The preparation of the work program shall include three elements of information: (1)	Enumeration of functions and objectives. The work program presentation shall begin with a brief paragraph defining and explaining the purposes, objectives and functions of the department or division. (2)	Service estimates and service standards. The work program shall contain a concise analysis of the level of services which can be provided with the funds included in the budget requests. Any inadequacies of service which are not provided for shall be pointed out, and any changes proposed in the level of services or activity shall be explained. (3)	Work load data. a.	The work program shall contain a tabular listing of the work load planned for the ensuing budget year. Department and division heads shall analyze each activity under their supervision and determine the significant work units in each. The work units shall be reflected in existing records or be easily countable. They shall reflect work effort and shall be stated in familiar terminology. b.	If program changes are requested for the ensuing budget year, the effect of the program change on work load output shall be estimated. (Code 1976, § 2-5031)
Sec. 2-542. - Budget requests. (a)	Persons making budget request shall:(1)	Read all budget instructions carefully;(2)	Meet all deadline dates;(3)	Check all figures for mathematical accuracy and totals; and(4)	Round off all figures to the nearest dollar, and omit all zeros in the cents columns.(b)	The budget requests shall be prepared in duplicate, the original and one copy; the original copy shall be returned to the finance department, and a copy shall be retained by the requesting department. (Code 1976, § 2-5032)
Sec. 2-543. - Preparation of schedules. (a)	Organization chart. (1)	Each department head shall summarize the department organization on the first sheet of the organization chart showing the major functional areas (to coincide with the currently established divisions of the department) and indicating the name of the function or division and the total full-time numbers of positions by each function or division. (2)	Additional sheets (one for each functional area or division) shall be included showing a detailed breakdown of each function or division, to include the total numbers of full-time positions for each classification or position title and the major functional areas under each division. (b)	Pricing schedule. (1)	The pricing schedule shall be provided prior to the start of the ensuing budget year. This schedule shall include costs (for budget purposes) for common items of equipment. (2)	Departmental officials shall contact the purchasing agent only for pricing estimates. The vendors shall not be contacted unless requested to do so by the city manager. (c)	Chart of accounts. The chart of accounts schedule shall be provided prior to the start of the ensuing budget year. This schedule shall name and describe all existing account classifications with the city. (Code 1976, § 2-5033)
Sec. 2-544. - Capital improvement program; definition. (a)	Capital improvements shall mean projects of generally large size, fixed nature and long life, value determined annually by the city's schedule for fees and capital projects on file in the office of the city clerk, which provide new or improved public facilities or services. Included in the first year of the program are all ongoing projects (those which have been funded), and those projects which are proposed to be funded for the ensuing fiscal year. All other proposed projects are scheduled over the remaining four years, in order of priority. (b)	Capital improvements shall include, without limitation, street improvements, bridges, water mains and treatment facilities, sewers (storm and sanitary), public buildings, parks, playgrounds, libraries, recreation facilities, the acquisition of land or right-of-way related to these projects, and major replacements and reconstruction. (c)	Also included as capital improvements are certain types of new major equipment. Generally, major equipment shall mean equipment with a life expectancy of at least 15 years. Heavy equipment shall include, without limitation, fire apparatus (these equipment items shall be included for new fire stations), bulldozers and draglines. (d)	Other items to be considered as capital improvements are preconstruction architectural and engineering costs and consultative services, such as site location studies, related to the planning and design of projects. (Code 1976, § 2-5034)Cross reference— Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 2-545. - General procedure for capital improvement programming. (a)	A determination shall be made for a five-year period of what capital improvements are needed or desirable, arranged in order of priority. Both uncompleted projects currently underway and newly proposed projects shall be included. (b)	The financial resources such as general obligation bonds and revenue bonds shall be analyzed to determine the funds which should be available or can be provided within safe limits for construction or completion of capital improvements during a five-year period. (c)	The first year of the five-year schedule, called the capital budget, is considered the capital budget for the current fiscal year and shall include only funded projects. (d)	Those new projects which are tentatively selected for construction as well as ongoing projects to be completed shall be scheduled over the remaining four-year period in accordance with their need and desirability and in direct relation to the funds available. (e)	At the end of each year the capital improvement program shall be reviewed. Any projects that are no longer justified or needed shall be eliminated; others may be shifted in position in the program in accordance with changing needs. An additional year shall be added to replace the year just completed. Projects included in the budget for the current year shall again appear in the first year of the five-year program; and new and additional projects shall fall somewhere within the remaining four years based upon consideration or priority, feasibility, and availability of funds. (f)	The criteria to be used in analyzing proposed projects and their relative importance and priority shall include, without limitation, the following: (1)	Protection of life;(2)	Maintenance of public health;(3)	Protection of property;(4)	Maintenance of physical property;(5)	Provision of public services;(6)	Replacement of obsolete facilities;(7)	Reduction of operating costs;(8)	Public convenience and comfort; and(9)	Enhancement of community appearance.(Code 1976, § 2-5035)
Sec. 2-546. - Completion of five-year capital improvement program estimates. (a)	Project proposal sheets shall be completed in duplicate. The original shall be provided to the budget division, forwarded to the city manager, and a copy shall be retained by the requesting department. (b)	All participating departmental officials shall receive copies of their respective five-year programs for the previous year that are to be used as department work copies. These copies shall be submitted to departmental officials along with the blank project proposal sheets which shall be used to complete the new five-year program. (c)	The work copies (previous year's program) shall be reviewed in detail to determine accuracy, completeness, etc.; and any revisions or corrections, shall be made. Projects which are no longer needed, or which are considered to be nonfeasible, etc., shall be eliminated. (d)	Project proposals shall be prepared for all new or additional projects. Information given for each project shall be developed as accurately and comprehensively as possible, including all applicable data elements as described in this section. (e)	Projects shall be arranged in priority sequence by year only; i.e., all projects scheduled to begin in the ensuing budget year shall be grouped together, followed by all projects scheduled in the subsequent budget year, etc. There is no need to rank projects within each year on the basis of priority. (f)	Cost information for prior expenditures shall be obtained from the finance department. This information shall be given for all projects where there have been expenditures. (g)	The financial portion of the project proposal sheet shall be completed, using the most accurate cost figures available. Previous expenditures shall be used in estimated costs. These figures shall be updated for current market conditions and prices. (Code 1976, § 2-5036)
Sec. 2-547. - Submittal of budget.     The annual operating budget for the city shall be submitted to the mayor and council for their final approval or disapproval no later than the regular midmonth meeting in June of each fiscal year. The final proposed budget shall be submitted to the members of the mayor and council for their review at least 30 days prior to that meeting. (Ord. No. 92-28, 7-23-1992)
Secs. 2-548—2-570. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 4. - INVESTMENT POLICY 
Sec. 2-571. - Definitions.     The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this division, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning:     Agencies means federal agency securities.     Asked means the price at which securities are offered.     Bankers' acceptance (BA) means a draft or exchange accepted by a bank or trust company. The accepting institution guarantees payment of the bill, as well as the issuer.     BID means the price offered by a buyer of securities. (When you are selling securities, you ask for a bid.) See definition of "Offer."     Broker means a person who brings buyers and sellers together for a commission.     Certificate of deposit (CD) means a time deposit with a specific maturity evidenced by a certificate. Large denomination CDs are typically negotiable.     Collateral means securities, evidence of deposit or other property which the borrower pledges to secure repayment of a loan. The term "collateral" also refers to securities pledged by a bank to secure deposits of public monies.     Comprehensive financial report (CAFR) means the official annual report for the city. The term "comprehensive financial report" includes five combined statements for each individual fund and account group prepared in conformity with GAAP. The term "comprehensive financial report" also includes supporting schedules necessary to demonstrate compliance with finance-related legal and contractual provisions, extensive introductory material and a detailed statistical section.     Coupon means: (1)	The annual rate of interest that a bond's issuer promises to pay the bondholder on the bond's face value. (2)	A certificate attached to a bond evidencing interest due on a payment date.    Dealer, as opposed to a broker, means a person who acts as a principal in all transactions, buying and selling for his own account.     Debenture means a bond secured only by the general credit of the issuer.     Delivery versus payment means two methods of delivery of securities: delivery versus payment and delivery versus receipt. The term "delivery versus payment" means delivery of securities with an exchange of money for the securities. The term "delivery versus receipt" means the delivery of securities with an exchange of a signed receipt for the securities.     Discount means the difference between the cost price of a security and its maturity when quoted at lower than face value. A security selling below the original offering price shortly after sale also is considered to be at a discount.     Discount securities means noninterest bearing money market instruments that are issued a discount and redeemed at maturity for full value, e.g., U.S. Treasury bills.     Diversification means dividing investment funds among a variety of securities offering independent returns.     Federal credit agencies means agencies of the federal government set up to supply credit to various classes of institutions, e.g., savings and loans, small business firms, students, farmers, farm cooperatives and exporters.     Federal Deposit Insurance Corporation (FDIC) means a federal agency that insures bank deposits up to $100,000.00 per deposit.     Federal home loan banks (FHLB) means the institutions that regulate and lend to savings and loan associations. The federal home loan banks play a role analogous to that played by the federal reserve banks vis-a-vis member commercial banks.     Federal National Mortgage Association (FNMA or Fannie Mae). Like GNMA, the FNMA was chartered under the Federal National Association Act of 1938. The term "FNMA" means a federal corporation working under the auspices of the department of housing and urban development (HUD), and is the largest single provider of residential mortgage funds in the United States. Fannie Mae is a private stockholder-owned corporation. The corporation's purchases include a variety of adjustable mortgages and second loans, in addition to fixed rate mortgages. FNMA's securities are also highly liquid and are widely accepted. FNMA assumes and guarantees that all security holders will receive timely payment of principal and interest.     Federal Open Market Committee (FOMC) consists of seven members of the federal reserve board and five of the 12 federal reserve presidents. The president of the New York Reserve Bank is a permanent member of the FOMC, while the other presidents serve on a rotating basis. The committee periodically meets to set federal reserve guidelines regarding purchases and sales of government securities in the open market as a means of influencing the volume of bank credit and money.     Federal reserve system means the central bank of the United States created by Congress and consisting of a seven-member board of governors in Washington, D.C., 12 regional banks and about 5,700 commercial banks that are members of the system.     Government National Mortgage Association (GNMA or Ginnie Mae) means securities influencing the volume of bank credit guaranteed by GNMA and issued by mortgage bankers, commercial banks, savings and loan associations and other institutions. The security holder is protected by the full faith and credit of the U.S. government. Ginnie Mae securities are backed by the FHA, VA or FMHM mortgages. The term "passthroughs" is often used to describe Ginnie Maes.     Liquidity means a liquid asset, which is an asset that can be converted easily and rapidly into cash without substantial loss of value. In the money market, a security is liquid if the spread between bid and asked prices narrow and reasonable size can be done at those quotes.     Local Government Investment Pool (LGIP) means the aggregate of all funds from political subdivisions that are placed in the custody of the state treasurer for investment and reinvestment.     Market value means the price at which a security is trading and could presumably be purchased or sold.     Master repurchase agreement means a written contract covering all future transactions between the parties to repurchase; reverse repurchase agreements that establishes each party's rights in the transactions. A master agreement will often specify, among other things, the buyer's right of the buyer-lender to liquidate the underlying securities in the event of default by the seller-borrower.     Maturity means the date upon which the principal or stated value of an investment becomes due and payable.     Money market means the market in which shortterm debt instruments (bills, commercial paper, bankers acceptances, etc.) are issued and traded.     Offer means the price asked by the seller of securities. (When you are buying securities, you ask for an offer.) (See the definitions of "Ask" and "Bid.")     Open market operations means purchases and sales of government and certain other securities in the open market by the New York Federal Reserve Bank as directed by the FOMC in order to influence the volume of money and credit in the economy. Purchases inject reserves into the bank system and stimulate growth of money and credit; sales have the opposite effect. Open market operations are the most flexible monetary policy tool.     Portfolio means a collection of securities held by an investor.     Primary dealer means a group of government security dealers who submit daily reports of market activity and positions and monthly financial statements to the Federal Reserve Bank of New York and are subject to its informal oversight. Primary dealers include the Securities and Exchange Commission (SEC), registered securities broker-dealers, banks and a few unregulated firms.     Prudent person rule means an investment standard. In some states the law requires that a fiduciary, such as a trustee, may invest money only in a list of securities selected by the custody state, the so called "legal list." In other states the trustee may invest in a security if such security is one which would be bought by a prudent person of discretion and intelligence who is seeking a reasonable income and preservation of capital.     Qualified public depositories means a financial institution which does not claim exemption from the payment of any sales or compensating use or ad valorem taxes under the laws of the state, which has segregated for the benefit of the commission eligible collateral having a value of not less than its maximum liability and which has been approved to hold public deposits by the public deposit protection commission.     Rate of return means the yield obtained on a security based on its purchase price.     Repurchase agreement (RP or REPO) means when a holder of securities sells such securities to an investor with an agreement to repurchase such securities at a fixed price on a fixed date. The security buyer in effect lends the seller money for the period of the agreement, and the terms of the agreement are structured to compensate him for such loan. Dealers use RP extensively to finance their positions, except when the FED is said to be doing RP, it is lending money, which is, increasing bank reserves.     Safekeeping means a service to customers rendered by banks for a fee whereby securities and valuables of all types and descriptions are held in the bank's vaults for protection.     Secondary market means a market made for the purchase and sale of outstanding issues following the initial distribution.     SEC Rule 15C3-1. See the definition of "Uniform net capital rule."     Securities and Exchange Commission (SEC) means an agency created by Congress to protect investors in securities transactions by administering securities legislation.     Treasury bill means a noninterest bearing discount security issued by the U.S. Treasury to finance the national debt. Most bills are issued to mature in three months, six months or one year.     Treasury bond means longterm U.S. Treasury securities having initial maturities of more than ten years.     Treasury note means a noninterest bearing discount security issued by the U.S. Treasury to finance the national debt. Most notes are issued to mature in three months, six months or one year.     Uniform net capital rule means a Securities and Exchange Commission requirement that member firms, as well as nonmember broker-dealers in securities, maintain a maximum ratio of indebtedness to liquid capital of 15:1; also called "net capital ratio." Indebtedness covers all money owed to a firm, including margin loans and commitments to purchase securities, one reason new public issues are spread among members of underwriting syndicates. Liquid capital includes cash and assets easily converted to cash.     Yield means the rate of annual income return on an investment, expressed as a percentage. (1)	Income yield is obtained by dividing the current dollar income by the current market price for the security. (2)	Net yield or yield to maturity means the current income yield minus any premium above par or plus any discount from par in the purchase price, with the adjustment spread over the period from the date of purchase to the date of maturity of the bond. (Ord. No. 2000-63, 9-7-2000)Cross reference— Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 2-572. - Policy.     It is the policy of the City of Valdosta (hereinafter referred to as the "city") to invest public funds in a manner which will provide the highest investment return with the maximum security while meeting the daily cash flow demands of the entity and in compliance with the provisions of O.C.G.A. § 36-83-4 and this Code governing the investment of public funds. (Ord. No. 2000-63, § 1.0, 9-7-2000)
Sec. 2-573. - Investment policy.     The city's investment policy shall be adopted by resolution of the city's mayor and council. The policy shall be reviewed annually by the finance director, external auditor and assistant finance director, and any modifications made to such policy must be approved by the city manager and the mayor and council. (Ord. No. 2000-63, § 18.0, 9-7-2000)
Sec. 2-574. - Scope of policy.     The city's investment policy applies to all financial assets of the city, except for the tree commission agency fund. Such funds are accounted for in the city's comprehensive annual financial report, and include: (1)	Funds: a.	General fund.b.	Special revenue funds.c.	Capital project funds.d.	Enterprise funds.e.	Internal service funds.f.	Trust and agency funds.g.	Other funds that may be created from time to time.(2)	Pooling of funds. Except for cash in certain restricted and special funds, the city will consolidate cash balances from all funds to maximize investments earnings. Investment income will be allocated to the various funds based on their respective participation and in accordance with generally accepted accounting principles. (Ord. No. 2000-63, § 2.0, 9-7-2000)
Sec. 2-575. - Prudence. (a)	Investments shall be made with judgment and care, under circumstances then prevailing, which persons of prudence, discretion and intelligence exercise in the management of their own affairs, not speculation, but for investment, considering the probable safety of their capital as well as the probable income derived. (b)	The standard of prudence to be used by investment officials shall be the prudent person standard, and shall be applied in the context of managing an overall portfolio. Investment officers acting in accordance with the written procedures and the investment policy and exercising due diligence shall be relieved of personal responsibility for an individual security's credit risk or market price changes, provided, deviations from expectations are reported in a timely fashion and appropriate action is taken to control adverse developments. (Ord. No. 2000-63, § 3.0, 9-7-2000)
Sec. 2-576. - Objectives.     The city's primary objectives, in the order of priority, for the investment activities shall be: (1)	Safety. Safety of principal is the foremost objective of the investment program. Investments of the city shall be undertaken in a manner that seeks to ensure the preservation of capital in the overall portfolio. The objective will be to mitigate credit and interest rate risks. (2)	Credit risk. The city will minimize credit risk, the risk of loss due to the failure of the security issuer or baker, by: a.	Limiting investments to the safest types of securities.b.	Prequalifying the financial institutions, broker/dealers, intermediaries and advisers with which the city will do business. c.	Diversifying the investment portfolio so that potential losses on individual securities will be minimized. (3)	Interest rate risk. The city will minimize the risk that the market value of securities in the portfolio will fall due to changes in general interest rates, by: a.	Structuring the investment portfolio so that securities mature to meet cash requirements for ongoing operations, thereby avoiding the need to sell securities on the open market prior to maturity. b.	Investing operating funds primarily in shorter-term securities, money market mutual funds or similar investment pools. (4)	Liquidity. The city's investment portfolio must be structured in a manner so as to provide sufficient liquidity to meet all operating requirements which might be reasonably anticipated. (5)	Return on investments. The city's investment portfolio shall be designed with the objective of attaining a rate of return throughout budgetary and economic cycles, commensurate with the city's cash flow characteristics of the portfolio. (Ord. No. 2000-63, § 4.0, 9-7-2000)
Sec. 2-577. - Delegation of authority. (a)	Authority to manage the city's investment program is derived from article I, section 1.1, Incorporation; name, corporate powers, of the city's Charter. (b)	The city and its inhabitants shall continue to be a body politic and corporate under the name of the City of Valdosta (hereinafter referred to as the "city"). The city shall be the legal continuation and successor to the city as heretofore incorporated, and shall continue to be vested with all property and rights of property which now belong to the city; shall have perpetual succession; may sue and be sued; may contract and be contracted with; may acquire and hold such property, real and personal, as may be devised, bequeathed, sold or in any manner conveyed or dedicated to or otherwise acquired by it, and from time to time may hold or invest, sell or dispose of any such property; may have a common seal and alter and renew such seal at will; may exercise, in conformity with the Charter, all municipal powers, functions, rights, privileges and immunities of every name and nature whatsoever. (c)	Management responsibility for the investment program is delegated to the finance director, who shall establish written procedures for the operation of the investment program consistent with this investment policy. Procedures should include reference to safekeeping, PSA repurchase agreements, banking service contracts and collateral/depository agreements. Such procedures shall include explicit delegation of authority to persons responsible for investment transactions. No person may engage in an investment transaction, except as provided under the terms of the policy set forth in this division and the procedures established by the finance director. The finance director shall be responsible for all transactions undertaken and shall establish a system of controls to regulate the activities of subordinate officials. (Ord. No. 2000-63, § 5.0, 9-7-2000)
Sec. 2-578. - Ethic and conflict of interest.     Officers and employees involved in the investment process shall refrain from personal business activity that could conflict with the proper execution of the investment program, or which could impair their ability to make impartial investment decisions. Employees and investment officials shall disclose to the city manager any material financial interests in financial institutions that conduct business within this jurisdiction, and they shall further disclose any large personal financial/investment positions that could be related to performance of the city, particularly with regard to the time of purchase and sales. (Ord. No. 2000-63, § 6.0, 9-7-2000)
Sec. 2-579. - Authorized financial dealers and institutions. (a)	A list will be maintained of financial institutions authorized to provide investment services. In addition, a list also will be maintained of approved security broker/dealers selected by creditworthiness (e.g., a minimum capital requirement of $10,000,000.00 and at least five years of operation). Such lists may include primary dealers or regional dealers that qualify under the Securities and Exchange Commission (SEC) Rule 15c3-1 (uniform capital rule). (b)	All financial institutions and broker/dealers who desire to become qualified for investment transactions must supply the following, as appropriate: (1)	Audited financial statements;(2)	Proof of National Association of Securities Dealers (NASD) certification;(3)	Proof of state registration;(4)	Completed broker/dealer questionnaire; and(5)	Certificate of having read and understood and agreeing to comply with the city's investment policy. An annual review of the financial condition and registration of qualified financial institutions and broker/dealers will be conducted by the finance director. (c)	Before accepting funds or engaging in investment transactions with the city, the supervising officer at each financial institution and recognized security broker/dealer shall submit a certification. Such document will certify that the officer has reviewed the investment policies and objectives, and agrees to disclose potential conflicts or risks to public funds that might arise out of business transactions between the firm/depository and the city. All financial institutions shall agree to undertake reasonable efforts to preclude imprudent transactions involving the city's funds. (d)	The supervising officer shall agree to exercise due diligence on monitoring the activities of the other officer and subordinate staff members engaged in transactions with the city. Employees of any firm or financial institution offering securities or investments to the city shall be trained in the precautions appropriate to public-sector investments and shall be required to familiarize themselves with the city's investment objectives, policies and constraints. (Ord. No. 2000-63, § 7.0, 9-7-2000)
Sec. 2-580. - Authorized and suitable investments.     The city is empowered by O.C.G.A. § 36-83-4 to invest in the following types of securities: (1)	Obligations of this state or other states.(2)	Obligations issued by the United States government:a.	U.S. Treasury bills.b.	U.S. Treasury notes.c.	U.S. Treasury bonds.(3)	Obligations fully insured or guaranteed by the United States government or a United States government agency: a.	Export-import bank.b.	Farmers' Home Administration.c.	General services administration.d.	Government National Mortgage Association (GNMA).e.	Penn Central Transportation Certificates.f.	Ship financing bonds, title 13.g.	Small Business Administration.h.	Washington Metropolitan Transit Authority bonds.(4)	Obligations of the following U.S. government agencies:a.	Federal Farm Credit Banks (FFCB).b.	Federal Home Loan Mortgage Corporation (FHLMC) participation certificates or debentures.c.	Federal Home Loan Bank (FHLB) or its banks.d.	Government National Mortgage Association (FNMA).e.	Federal National Mortgage Association (FNMA) participation certificates or debentures which are guaranteed by GNMA. f.	Student Loan Marketing Association.(5)	Repurchase agreements backed by subsections (2), (3) and (4) of this section.(6)	Prime bankers' acceptance (bankers' acceptances that are eligible for purchase by the Federal Reserve Bank and have a letter of credit rating of A+ or better). (7)	The local government investment pool.(8)	Obligations of other political subdivisions of the state.(9)	Time deposits and saving deposits of banks organized under the laws of the state or the U.S. government and operating in the state: a.	Savings accounts.b.	Money market accounts.c.	Certificates of deposit (nonnegotiable type).(Ord. No. 2000-63, § 8.0, 9-7-2000)
Sec. 2-581. - Collateralization. (a)	Collateralization will be required on two types of investments:(1)	Certificate of deposit; and(2)	Repurchase and reverse agreements.(b)	In order to anticipate market changes and provide a level of security for all funds, the collateralization level will be 100 percent of the market value of principal and accrued interest. The city chooses to limit collateral to: (1)	Obligations issued by the United States government.(2)	Obligations fully insured or guaranteed by the United States government or a United States government agency. (3)	Obligations of the following U.S. government agencies:a.	Federal farm credit banks (FFCB).b.	Federal Home Loan Mortgage Corporation (FHLMC).c.	Federal Home Loan Bank (FHLB) or its banks.d.	Government National Mortgage Association (GNMA).e.	Federal National Mortgage Association (FNMA) participation certificates or debentures which are guaranteed by GNMA. f.
