Student Loan Marketing Association.(4)	Collateral will always be held by an independent third party with whom the city has a current custodian agreement. (5)	A clearly marked evidence of ownership (safekeeping receipt) must be supplied to the city and retained. (Ord. No. 2000-63, § 9.0, 9-7-2000)
Sec. 2-582. - Safekeeping and custody.     All securities transactions, including collateral for repurchase agreements, entered into by the city shall be conducted on a delivery-versus-payment (DVP) basis. Securities will be held by a third party custodian designated by the finance director and evidenced by safekeeping receipts. (Ord. No. 2000-63, § 10.0, 9-7-2000)
Sec. 2-583. - Diversification. (a)	The city will diversify its investments by security type and institution. With the exception of U.S. Treasury securities, no more than 50 percent of the city's total investment portfolio will be invested with a single financial institution. (b)	The following guidelines represent maximum limits established for diversification by instrument: U.S. Treasury obligations100 percentU.S. government agency securities and securities issued by instrumentalities of government-sponsored corporations  75 percentRepurchase agreements 25 percentPrime bankers acceptance 10 percentLocal government investment pool 40 percentCertificates of deposit 25 percentObligations of other political subdivisions of the state 25 percent (Ord. No. 2000-63, § 11.0, 9-7-2000)
Sec. 2-584. - Maximum maturities. (a)	To the extent possible, the city shall attempt to match its investments with anticipated cash flow requirements. Unless such investments are matched to a specific cash flow, the city will not directly invest in securities maturing more than five years from the date of purchase. The city shall adopt a weighted average maturity limitation (which often range from 90 days to three years), consistent with the city's investment objectives. (b)	Reserve or other funds with longer term investment horizons may be invested in securities exceeding five years if the maturities of such investments are made to coincide as nearly as practicable with the expected use of funds. The intent to invest in securities with longer maturities shall be disclosed in writing to the mayor and council. (c)	Because inherent difficulties in accurately forecasting cash flow requirements, a portion of the portfolio should be continuously invested in readily available funds to assure that appropriate liquidity is maintained in order to meet ongoing obligations. (Ord. No. 2000-63, § 12.0, 9-7-2000)
Sec. 2-585. - Internal controls.     The quarterly and annual investment reports submitted to the mayor and council shall contain sufficient information to permit an independent organization to evaluate the performance of the investment program. Every year, the city shall retain an independent firm to evaluate investment performance and conduct an operational audit. The purchase of such examinations shall be to obtain suggestions for improved future performance, and to verify that investment officials have acted in accordance with the investment policy and written investment procedures. The compensation structure for investment officials shall be designed to provide adequate compensation in the event of successful performance without encouraging a bias toward risk. (Ord. No. 2000-63, § 13.0, 9-7-2000)
Sec. 2-586. - Performance standards. (a)	Investment portfolio. The investment portfolio will be managed in accordance with the parameters specified within the policy set forth in this division. The portfolio should obtain a market average rate of return during a market/economic environment of stable interest rates. A series of appropriate benchmarks shall be established against which portfolio performance shall be compared on a regular basis. (b)	Market value of portfolio. The market value of the portfolio shall be calculated at least quarterly and a statement of the market value of the portfolio shall be issued at least quarterly. This will ensure that review of the investment portfolio, in terms and value and price volatility, has been performed consistent with the Governmental Finance Officers Association's (GFOA) recommended practice on mark to market practices for state and local government investment portfolios and investment pools. (c)	Yield. The investment portfolio shall be designed with the objective of attaining a market rate of return throughout budgetary and economic cycles, taking into account the investment risk constraints and liquidity needs. Return on investment is of secondary importance compared to the safety and liquidity objectives described in section 2-576. The core of investments are limited to relative low risk securities in anticipation of earning a fair return relative to the risk being assumed. Securities shall not be sold prior to maturity with the following exceptions: (1)	A security with declining credit may be sold to minimize loss of principal.(2)	A security swap would improve the quality, yield or target duration in the portfolio.(3)	Liquidity needs of the portfolio require that a security be sold.(Ord. No. 2000-63, § 14.0, 9-7-2000)
Sec. 2-587. - Reporting.     The investment officer shall prepare an investment report at least quarterly, including a management summary that provides for an analysis of the status of the current investment portfolio and transactions made over the last quarter. Such management summary will be prepared in a manner which will allow the city to ascertain whether investment activities during the reporting period have conformed to the investment policy. The report should be provided to the city manager, finance director, legislative body and any pool participant. The report will include the following: (1)	Listing of individual securities held at the end of the reporting period.(2)	Realized and unrealized gains or losses resulting from appreciation or depreciation by listing the cost and market value of the securities over one year in duration that are not intended to be held until maturity (in accordance with Governmental Accounting Standards Board (GASB) requirements). (3)	Average weighted yield to maturity of portfolio on investments as compared to applicable benchmarks. (4)	Listing of investments by maturity date.(5)	Percentage of the total portfolio which each type of investment represents.(Ord. No. 2000-63, § 15.0, 9-7-2000)
Sec. 2-588. - Policy considerations. (a)	Exemption. Any investment currently held that does not meet the guidelines of the policy set forth in this division shall be exempted from the requirements of such policy. At maturity or liquidation, such monies shall be reinvested only as provided by this division. (b)	Amendments. The policy set forth in this division shall be reviewed on an annual basis. Any changes must be approved by the investment officer and any other appropriate authority, as well as individuals charged with maintaining internal controls. (Ord. No. 2000-63, § 16.0, 9-7-2000)
Sec. 2-589. - List of documents.     The following documents, as applicable, are on file in the office of the city clerk: (1)	Listing of authorized personnel;(2)	Relevant investment statutes and ordinances;(3)	Repurchase agreements and tri-party agreements;(4)	Listing of authorized broker/dealers and financial institutions;(5)	Safekeeping agreements;(6)	Sample investment reports; and(7)	Methodology for calculating rate of return.(Ord. No. 2000-63, § 17.0, 9-7-2000)Editor's note— The documents listed in this section are on file in the office of the city clerk, and are incorporated into this section as if fully set out. 
Secs. 2-590—2-610. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 5. - DEBT MANAGEMENT POLICY 
Sec. 2-611. - Purpose.     The city recognizes the foundation of any well managed debt program is a comprehensive debt policy. A debt policy sets forth the parameters for issuing debt and managing outstanding debt, and provides guidance to decision makers regarding the timing and purposes for which debt may be issued, types and amounts of permissible debt, method of sale that may be used and structural features that may be incorporated. The debt policy should recognize a binding commitment to full and timely repayment of all debt as an intrinsic requirement for entry into the capital markets. Adherence to a debt policy helps to ensure that a government maintains a sound debt position and that credit quality is protected. Advantages of a debt policy are that it: (1)	Enhances the quality of decisions by imposing order and discipline, and promoting consistency and continuity in decision making; (2)	Rationalizes the decision making process;(3)	Identifies objectives for staff to implement;(4)	Demonstrates a commitment to longterm financial planning objectives; and(5)	Is regarded positively by the rating agencies in reviewing credit quality.(Ord. No. 2000-64, § I, 9-7-2000)
Sec. 2-612. - Adoption.     The city's debt policy shall be adopted by resolution of the city's mayor and council. The policy shall be reviewed annually by the finance director, external auditor and the assistant finance director, and any modifications made to the policy must be approved by the city manager, mayor and council. (Ord. No. 2000-64, § XIV, 9-7-2000)
Sec. 2-613. - Responsibility for developing financing recommendations. (a)	The primary responsibility for developing financing recommendations rests with the finance director. In developing such recommendations, the finance director shall be assisted by the assistant finance director, budget director and accounting manager, the four of whom shall comprise a debt management committee. The responsibilities of the debt management committee shall be to: (1)	Meet no less than quarterly to consider the need for financing and assess progress on the capital improvement program; (2)	Meet, as necessary, in preparation for a financing, review changes in state and federal legislation; (3)	Annually review the provisions of ordinances authorizing issuance of obligations; and (4)	Annually review services provided by the financial advisor, bond counsel, paying agent and other service providers to evaluate the extent and effectiveness of services being provided. (b)	Prior to the quarterly meeting, the assistant finance director and budget director shall jointly prepare a written report on the status of capital improvement program financing. The report shall be based in part on information collected from the primary capital improvement project managers in the city, and shall include a projection of near term financing needs compared to available resources, an analysis of the impact of contemplated financings on the property tax rate and user charges, and a financing recommendation. (c)	In developing financing recommendations, the debt management committee shall consider:(1)	The time proceeds of obligation are expected to remain on hand and the related carrying cost; (2)	The options for interim financing, including shortterm and interfund borrowing, taking into consideration federal and state reimbursement regulations; (3)	The effect of proposed action on the tax rate and user charges;(4)	Trends in interest rates;(5)	Other factors, as appropriate.(Ord. No. 2000-64, § II, 9-7-2000)
Sec. 2-614. - Bond counsel involvement.     The bond counsel will issue an opinion as to the legality and tax exempt status of any obligations. The city will also seek the advice of bond counsel on all other types of financings, and on any other questions involving federal tax or arbitrage law. The bond counsel is also responsible for the preparation of the ordinance authorizing issuance of obligations and all of the closing documents to complete their sale and will perform other services as defined by contract approved by the city council. (Ord. No. 2000-64, § II, 9-7-2000)
Sec. 2-615. - Financial advisor involvement.     When necessary, the city will seek the advice of the financial advisor. The financial advisor will advise the city on the structuring of obligations to be issued, inform the city of various options, advise the city as to how choices will impact the marketability of city obligations and provide other services as defined by contract approved by the city council. To ensure independence, the financial advisor will not bid on nor underwrite any city debt issues. The financial advisor will inform the city manager of significant issues. (Ord. No. 2000-64, § II, 9-7-2000)
Sec. 2-616. - Limitations on indebtedness. (a)	Established. The city will keep outstanding debt within the limits prescribed by state statute and at levels consistent with its creditworthiness objectives. The city will annually identify intermediate-range to long-range capital spending and debt conditions that would impact city residents' property taxes, and fit proposed spending to the city's debt management goals. The city will exchange information and expertise with each jurisdiction of the county during each jurisdiction's capital improvement budgeting process so that the jurisdictions can eliminate duplication, share facilities, where appropriate, and provide the taxpayers with the greatest return for the jurisdictions' capital improvement. (b)	Target limitations on nonself-supporting tax general obligation indebtedness; full faith and credit lease-purchase obligations. (1)	As a matter of policy, the city shall conduct its finances so that the amount of direct, nonself-supporting tax general obligation debt and full faith and credit lease-purchase obligations outstanding at any time does not exceed one percent of the city's taxable assessed valuation. Furthermore, the city shall strive to limit annual debt service requirements on such obligations to an amount that is not greater than ten percent of annual general fund revenues. (2)	Such limitations shall apply to debt obligations secured by a pledge of the city's full faith and credit obligations which are not self-supporting, or which are paid from the general fund revenues. (c)	Target limitations on lease-purchase financing of equipment and furnishings. The city may enter into shortterm lease-purchase obligations to finance the acquisition capital equipment and furnishings with estimated lives of less than ten years. Outstanding lease-purchase obligations issued to finance capital equipment and furnishings shall not exceed 0.125 percent of the city's taxable assessed valuation. Repayment of such lease-purchase obligations shall occur over a period not to exceed the useful life of the underlying asset or in any case no longer than five years from the date of such obligations. The debt management committee shall be responsible for developing procedures for use by city departments interested in participating in the lease-purchase program, and for setting repayment terms and amortization schedules, in consultation with participating departments. (d)	Limitations on general fund loan guarantees and credit support. (1)	As part of the city's financing activities, general fund resources may be used to provide credit support or loan guarantees for public and private developments that meet high priority city needs. Before such general fund commitments are made, specific policy goals and objectives that determine the nature and type of projects qualifying for support, and specific limitations to be placed on the maximum amount of general fund resources pledged to such projects shall be developed. The department of finance shall be responsible for coordinating the development of such policies and goals, which shall not take effect until approved by the city council. General fund loan guarantees shall be subject to the overall debt limitations set forth in subsection (b) of this section. (2)	Recognizing the limited capacity of the city's general fund to support both ongoing operating programs and secure longterm debt obligations, use of the general fund to secure such obligations must first be approved by the debt management committee. Key factors that will be considered in determining whether or not the general fund should be used to secure a particular debt obligation will include the following: a.	Demonstration of underlying self-support, thus limiting potential general fund financial exposure. b.	Use of general fund support as a transition to a fully stand alone credit structure, where interim use of general fund credit support reduces borrowing costs and provides a credit history for new or hard to establish credits. c.	General fund support is determined by the city council to be in the city's overall best interest. (e)	Target limitations on the issuance of revenue-secured debt obligations. The city shall seek to finance the capital needs of its revenue producing enterprise activities through the issuance of revenue-secured debt obligations. Prior to issuing revenue-secured debt obligations, city departments, in consultation with the finance director, will develop financial plans and projections showing the feasibility of the planned financing, required rates and charges needed to support the planned financing, and the impact of the planned financing on ratepayers, property owners, city departments and other affected parties. The amount of revenue-secured debt obligations issued by a city department will be limited by the feasibility of the overall financing plan as determined by the debt management committee. Revenue-secured debt obligations must first be reviewed and approved by the debt management committee before being issued. (Ord. No. 2000-64, § III, 9-7-2000)
Sec. 2-617. - Structure and term of indebtedness. (a)	Rapidity of debt repayment. Generally, borrowing of the city should be of a duration that does not exceed the economic life of the improvement that such borrowing finances and, where feasible, should be shorter than the projected economic life. Moreover, to the extent possible, the city should design the repayment of debt so as to rapidly recapture its credit capacity for future use. The city shall strive to repay the principal amount of its longterm general obligation debt by at least 20 percent in five years and 40 percent in ten years. The city may choose to structure debt repayment so as to wraparound existing obligations or achieve other financing planning goals. Such alternative structures shall be subject to the approval of the debt policy committee, in consultation with the involved city departments, before being recommended to the city manager and city council. (b)	Use of variable rate securities. When appropriate, the city may choose to issue securities that pay a rate of interest that varies according to a predetermined formula or results from a periodic remarketing of the securities. The decision to issue such securities must be reviewed and approved by the debt management committee and city manager before the council is requested to approve the issuance of such securities. (c)	Pledge of restricted funds to secure debt. The city has the power to make an irrevocable pledge of a security interest in an account created exclusively for the security holders of the city obligations. Before such funds are used to secure a prospective financing, policies regarding the use of such restricted funds shall be developed by the debt management committee to ensure that each use of such funds to secure bonds does not violate restrictions on such funds and that the underlying program commitments can be maintained in addition to meeting debt service obligations on debt secured by the restricted funds. Such policies shall be presented as recommendations to the city manager, then to the council prior to or at the time issuance of the secured debt is to be authorized. (d)	Use of subordinate lien obligations. Creation of a subordinate lien financing structure, if appropriate, shall be based on the overall financing needs of a particular department, expected credit ratings, relative cost of subordinate lien structure and impacts on the city as determined by the debt management committee, in consultation with the involved department. The results of such review shall be presented in the form of recommendations to the city manager, then to the mayor and council for consideration prior to or at the time such bonds are being authorized. (Ord. No. 2000-64, § IV, 9-7-2000)
Sec. 2-618. - Creditworthiness objectives.     Considering other components of the guidelines set forth in this division, the city's primary objective is to minimize debt service costs. To measure and compare the cost of alternatives, the city will use net present value and internal rate-of-return analysis. Such objective will be achieved through the following: (1)	Credit ratings. The city seeks to maintain the highest possible credit ratings for all categories of shortterm and longterm general obligation and revenue debt that can be achieved without compromising delivery of basic city services and achievement of adopted city policy objectives. The city recognizes that external economic, natural or other events may from time to time affect the creditworthiness of the city's debt. Nevertheless, the executive and legislative departments are committed to ensuring that actions within their control are prudent. (2)	Rating agency relationships. The debt management committee shall be responsible for maintaining relationships with the rating agencies that currently assign ratings to the city's various debt obligations. Such effort shall include providing periodic updates on the city's general financial condition along with coordinating meetings and presentations in conjunction with a new debt issuance. (3)	Use of rating agencies. The debt management committee shall be responsible for determining whether or not a rating shall be requested on a particular financing, and which of the major rating agencies shall be asked to provide such rating. (4)	Minimum longterm rating requirements. The city's minimum rating requirement for its direct, longterm debt obligations is a rating of "A" or higher. If such a longterm debt obligation cannot meet such requirement based on its underlying credit strength, then credit enhancement shall be sought to ensure that the minimum rating is achieved. If credit enhancement is unavailable, or is determined by the debt management committee to be uneconomic, then the obligations may be issued without a rating. A lower rating standard may be accepted for indirect or conduit obligations, subject to the approval of the debt management committee. (5)	Financial disclosure. a.	The city is committed to full and complete financial disclosure, and to fully cooperating with rating agencies, institutional and individual investors, city departments and agencies, other levels of government and the general public to share clear, comprehensible and accurate financial information. The city is committed to meeting secondary disclosure requirements on a timely and comprehensive basis. b.	Official statements accompanying debt issues, comprehensive annual financial reports and continuous disclosure statements will meet, at a minimum, the standards articulated by the Municipal Standards Rulemaking Board (MSBR), the Government Accounting Standards Board (GASB), the National Federation of Municipal Analysts, the Securities and Exchange Commission (SEC) and generally accepted accounting principles (GAAP). The department of finance shall be responsible for ongoing disclosures to establish national information repositories and for maintaining compliance with disclosure standards promulgated by state and national regulatory bodies. (6)	Credit enhancements. Credit enhancements (letters of credit, bond insurance, etc.), may be used, but only when net debt service on the bonds is reduced by more than the costs of the enhancements. Selection of credit enhancement providers shall be subject to a competitive bid process developed by the debt management committee. (7)	Capital planning. To enhance creditworthiness and prudent financial management, the city is committed to systematic capital planning, intergovernmental cooperation and coordination, and longterm financial planning. Evidence of such commitment to systematic capital planning will be demonstrated through adoption of the annual capital improvement plans (CIP). (Ord. No. 2000-64, § V, 9-7-2000)
Sec. 2-619. - Method of sale. (a)	Determination of best sale method. In connection with the issuance of each debt obligation, the city shall determine the best sale method, giving consideration to: (1)	Financial market conditions;(2)	Issue-specific conditions, such as the type and life of the financed projects and issue size; (3)	The costs and risks associated with alternative debt structures; and(4)	City-related conditions, including its credit rating, general financial condition and staff capability to administer the financing. In all instances, the city shall promote competition in issuing debt. Such promotion will be implemented in the selection of professionals and other service providers, giving consideration to the experience and quality of service, as well as cost. In determining whether to sell the debt on a negotiated or competitive basis, the factors outlined in the Government Finance Officers Association's recommended practice on selecting and managing the method of sale will be followed. (b)	Competitive sale. As a matter of policy, the city shall seek to issue its debt obligations in a competitive sale unless it is determined by the debt management committee that such a sale method will not produce the best results for the city. In such instances where the city, in a competitive bidding for its debt securities (whether general obligation or nongeneral obligation debt), deems the bids received as unsatisfactory or does not receive bids, it may enter into negotiation for the sale of securities. (c)	Negotiated sale. When determined appropriate and approved by the debt management committee, the city may elect to sell its debt obligations through a negotiated sale. Such determination may be made on an issue-by-issue basis for a series of issues or for part or all of a specific financing program. Selection of the underwriting team shall be made pursuant to selection procedures set forth in this division, consistent with this Code. (d)	Private placement. When determined and approved by the debt management committee, the city may select to sell its debt obligations through a private placement or limited public offering. Selection of a placement agent shall be made pursuant to selection procedures developed by the debt management committee, consistent with this Code. (e)	Official bid form. The city shall design an official bid form to be made a part of each official notice of sale published in conjunction with the sale of debt securities in a competitive sale by the city. (Ord. No. 2000-64, § VI, 9-7-2000)
Sec. 2-620. - Shortterm debt and interim financing. (a)	Lines of credit. Where their use is judged by the debt management committee to be prudent and advantageous to the city, the city has the power to enter into agreements with commercial banks or other financial entities for the purpose of acquiring lines or letters of credit that shall provide the city with access to credit under the terms and conditions as specified in such agreements. Before entering into any such agreements, takeout financing for such letters of credit must be planned for and determined to be feasible by the debt management committee. Any agreements with financial institutions for the acquisition of lines or letters of credit shall be approved by the mayor and council. Lines and letters of credit entered into by the city shall be in the support of projects contained in the approved capital improvement plan. (b)	Bond anticipation notes. Where their use is judged by the debt management committee to be prudent and advantageous to the city, the city may choose to issue bond anticipation notes as a source of interim construction financing. Before issuing such notes, takeout financing for such notes must be planned for and determined to be feasible by the debt management committee. Bond anticipation notes may be sold in either a competitive or negotiated sale, subject to authorization and approval of the mayor and council. (c)	Tax and revenue anticipation notes. Where their use is judged by the debt management committee to be prudent and advantageous to the city, the city may choose to issue tax and revenue anticipation notes to fund internal working capital cashflow needs. Before issuing such notes, cashflow projections will be prepared by the appropriate city departments and reviewed by the debt management committee. Tax and revenue anticipation notes may be sold in either a competitive or negotiated sale, subject to authorization and approval by the city council. (d)	Tax exempt commercial paper. The city may choose to issue tax exempt commercial paper as a source of interim construction financing for projects contained in the city's approved capital improvement plan only after the debt management committee determines that such a financing represents the least cost interim financing option for the city. Furthermore, tax exempt commercial paper shall not be issued for city capital programs unless it is of sufficient economic size as determined by the debt management committee. A report recommending the issuance of tax exempt commercial paper must first be approved by the debt management committee before recommendations are made to the city council authorizing the establishment of such a program. (Ord. No. 2000-64, § VII, 9-7-2000)
Sec. 2-621. - Refunding of indebtedness. (a)	Debt service savings—Advance refundings. The city may issue advance refunding bonds (as defined for federal tax law purposes) when advantageous, legally permissible, prudent and net present value savings, expressed as a percentage of the par amount of the refunding bonds, equal or exceed five percent. Exceptions to such requirement shall be made only upon the approval of the debt management committee. (b)	Same—Current refundings. The city may issue current refunding bonds (as defined for federal tax law purposes) when advantageous, legally permissible, prudent and net present value savings equal or exceed $100,000.00. (c)	Restructuring of debt. The city may choose to refund outstanding indebtedness when existing bond covenants or other financial structures impinge on prudent and sound financial management. Savings requirements for current or advance refundings undertaken to restructure debt may be waived by the debt management committee upon a finding that such a restructuring is in the city's overall best financial interests. (d)	Open market purchase of city securities. The city may choose to defease its outstanding indebtedness through purchases of its securities on the open market when market conditions make such an option financially feasible. The debt management committee shall be responsible for developing procedures for executing open market purchases and the savings objectives to be achieved by undertaking such actions. (Ord. No. 2000-64, § VIII, 9-7-2000)
Sec. 2-622. - Rebate reporting and covenant compliance.     The debt management committee shall establish a system of recordkeeping and reporting to meet the arbitrage rebate compliance requirements of the federal tax code. Such effort shall include tracking investment earnings on bond proceeds, calculating rebate payments in compliance with tax law and remitting any rebatable earnings to the federal government in a timely manner in order to preserve the tax-exempt status of the city's outstanding debt issues. Additionally, general financial reporting and certification requirements embodied in bond covenants shall be monitored to ensure that all covenants are complied with. (Ord. No. 2000-64, § IX, 9-7-2000)
Sec. 2-623. - Conduit financings.     The city may sponsor conduit financings for those activities (i.e., economic development, housing, health facilities, etc.) that have a general public purpose and are consistent with the city's overall service and policy objectives as determined by the mayor and council. All conduit financings must completely insulate the city from any credit risk or exposure, and must first be approved by the debt management committee before being submitted to the city manager, then to the city council for authorization and implementation. (Ord. No. 2000-64, § X, 9-7-2000)
Sec. 2-624. - Financing proposals.     Any capital financing proposal made to a city department, agency or commission involving a pledge or other extension of the city's credit through the sale of securities, execution of loans or leases, or making of guarantees or otherwise directly or indirectly involving the lending or pledging of the city's credit shall be referred to the debt management committee, who, in a timely manner, shall be responsible for analyzing the proposal, responding to the proposal and recommending to the city manager the required action to be taken. (Ord. No. 2000-64, § XI, 9-7-2000)
Sec. 2-625. - Derivative products.     The city may, in the future, choose to enter into contracts and financing agreements involving interest rate swaps, floating/fixed rate auction or reset securities, or other forms of debt bearing synthetically determined interest rates as authorized under state statutes. Before entering into such contracts or agreements, a review team made up of the debt management committee and appropriate department staff and outside consultants shall be formed to review the risks and benefits of such financing techniques and expected impacts on the city's longterm financial operations and credit ratings. When completed, the report shall be presented to the city manager, then to the city council for authorization and implementation. (Ord. No. 2000-64, § XII, 9-7-2000)
Sec. 2-626. - Selection of finance consultants and service providers.     The city's finance director shall be responsible for establishing a solicitation and selection process for securing professional services that are required to develop and implement the city's debt program. Goals of the solicitation and selection process shall include encouraging participation from both local and national qualified service providers, and securing services at competitive prices. (1)	Bond counsel. As part of its responsibility to oversee and coordinate the marketing of all city indebtedness, the city attorney, with the advice of the debt management committee and a committee representing city departments, agencies and commissions with capital financing needs, shall make recommendations to the city manager, then to the city council regarding the selection of bond counsel to be employed and the duration of the employment for individual financing or a series of financings. The solicitation and selection process for such services will comply with requirements of this Code for professional, technical and expert services. The council shall make such selection, taking into consideration such recommendations. (2)	Underwriters. The finance director shall solicit proposals for underwriting services for all debt issued in a negotiated or private placement sale mode. The solicitation process used for such services shall fully comply with requirements of this Code for professional, technical and expert services, and the debt management committee shall evaluate written proposals and, if deemed necessary, conduct oral interviews. In addition, the proposal solicitation and selection process for negotiated sales as developed by the debt management committee, and amended from time to time, shall also be followed. The selection of underwriters may be for an individual financing, a series of financings or a specified period of time. The council shall make such selections, taking into consideration the recommendations of the review committee. (3)	Financial advisor. The finance director, with the advice of the debt management committee and the city department, agencies and commissions with capital financing needs, shall make recommendations to the city manager, then to the city council regarding the selection of financial advisors to be employed and the duration of such employment. The solicitation and selection process for such services will comply with the requirements of this Code for professional, technical and expert services. The time period for employment may relate to an individual financing, a series of financings or a specified period of time. (4)	Paying agent. The finance director shall periodically solicit for paying agent services from qualified commercial and trustee banks. The cost of providing such services shall be used by the debt management committee, along with other qualitative measurements, in developing a paying agent recommendation to the city council, along with the term of such agreement. (5)	Other service providers. The finance director shall periodically solicit for other service providers (escrow agents, verification agents, trustees, etc.). The cost of providing such services shall be used by the debt management committee in developing a recommendation to the city manager, then to the city council, along with the term of such agreement. (Ord. No. 2000-64, § XIII, 9-7-2000)
Sec. 2-627. - Annual audit.     The annual audit of the city shall describe in detail all funds and fund balances established as part of any direct debt financing of the city. The audit may also contain a report detailing any material or rate covenants contained in any direct offering of the city and whether or not such covenants have been satisfied. (Ord. No. 2000-64, § XIV, 9-7-2000)
Secs. 2-628—2-650. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 6. - CASH HANDLING POLICY 
Sec. 2-651. - Definitions.     The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this division, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning:     Cash means currency, coins, checks, money orders, traveler's checks, ACH payments and credit card payments.     Casual collection point means a location where cash is collected which is not designated as a cash collection point by the finance department, including, but not limited to, road race registration sites, auction sites and after school program sites. (Ord. No. 2000-65, 9-7-2000)Cross reference— Definitions generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 2-652. - Adoption.     The city's cash handling policy shall be adopted by resolution of the mayor and council. The policy shall be reviewed annually by the finance director, external auditor and the assistant finance director and any modifications made to such policy must be approved by the city manager, mayor and council. (Ord. No. 2000-65, 9-7-2000)
Sec. 2-653. - Policy statement.     Strong internal controls for cash collection are necessary to prevent mishandling of city funds and are designed to safeguard and protect employees from inappropriate charges of mishandling funds by defining their responsibilities in the cash handling process. The city cash handling policy requires that areas receiving cash be approved by the finance director and be designated as cash collection points. The term "cash collection point" means a department or other entity that handles cash on a regular basis. Although departments and other entities with casual cash collections are not recognized as cash collection points, they must follow the same cash handling policies and procedures that apply to the cash collection points. Required policies for cash collection points include the following: (1)	Accounting for cash as such cash is received.(2)	Adequate separation of duties.(3)	Proper prenumbered receipts for any cash received.(4)	Approval of any voided cash receipts with the initials of the approving supervisor.(5)	Adequate safeguards for handling and storing cash.(6)	Daily depositing monies received in the form and amounts received.(Ord. No. 2000-65, 9-7-2000)
Sec. 2-654. - Knowledge of policy.     Any department head or supervisor with responsibilities for managing city cash receipts and employees who are entrusted with the receipt, deposit and reconciliation of cash for city-related activities should know the cash handling policy set forth in this division. (Ord. No. 2000-65, 9-7-2000)
Sec. 2-655. - Responsibilities. (a)	Cash collection point supervisor. The responsibilities of the cash collection point supervisor shall be to: (1)	Design an adequate separation of duties in cash handling.(2)	Develop a method of accounting for cash as it is received.(3)	Provide adequate safeguards for cash.(4)	Inform the accounting office of any changes in cash handling procedures or personnel involved with the cash collection point. (5)	Balance collections at the end of each business day.(b)	Cash collection point cashiers. The responsibilities of the cash collection point cashier shall be to: (1)	Conduct cash transactions with customers.(2)	Upon receipt, immediately mark checks with the customer's account number or general ledger account number. (3)	Count the cash and turn it over to the deposit preparer at the end of the shift.(4)	Turn over any supporting documentation to the cash collection point supervisor.(c)	Deposit preparer. The responsibilities of the deposit preparer shall be to: (1)	Count the cash receipts and verify check totals, prepare the deposit and deliver or have the deposit delivered to the bank. (2)	Store the cash in a safe or other secure place until such cash is deposited.(Ord. No. 2000-65, 9-7-2000)
Sec. 2-656. - Establishing new cash collection points.     The finance director must authorize all new cash collection points before collection begins. Departments or other entities wishing to become cash collection points must submit a request to the finance director. Such request must include the following: (1)	Reasons why a cash collection point is needed.(2)	A list of persons involved with the cash collection point and a description of such persons' duties. (3)	Whether there is a need for a change advance.(4)	A description of the reconciliation process, including the frequency of reconciliation.(5)	A description of the security for safeguarding cash until such cash is deposited.The request will be reviewed and, if appropriate, approved by the finance director. (Ord. No. 2000-65, 9-7-2000)
Sec. 2-657. - Operating procedures for cash collection points.     The following procedures shall be required for the operation of cash collection points: (1)	All cash received must be recorded through a cash register or computer terminal, when available, and/or the customer should be given a prenumbered receipt form with a duplicate record being retained from the receiving department. Receipts should be put in numerical order at the end of each shift. (2)	All numbered receipts must be accounted for, including voided receipts. Approved prenumbered receipts are available at customer service. Rediform receipts are not acceptable. (3)	The cash collection point must maintain a clear separation of duties. An individual should not have the responsibility for more than one of the cash handling components (collecting, reconciling or depositing). (4)	The cash received must be reconciled to the cash register tape, computer terminal edit or prenumbered receipts at the end of the day or at the end of each shift. (5)	All checks, cash and credit card receipts must be stored in a safe or other secure place until deposited. (6)	Checks must be made payable to the city and then restrictively endorsed for deposit to the city. (7)	Cash collection points must not cash checks unless the finance director has granted prior approval. (8)	All funds must be deposited intact, and not intermingled or substituted with other funds. However, checks issued incorrectly may be returned to the payer. (9)	Refunds must be made by city check.(10)	Payments must not be made from funds collected. All collected funds and request checks for payments shall be deposited. Other than official petty cash funds, there should be no exception to the policy set forth in this subsection. (11)	If a petty cash fund is maintained, it shall be an official fund and funds that have been held back for such purpose. (12)	If a cash collection point experiences a loss or theft, the finance director should be notified at once. The finance director will notify the police of such loss or theft. (13)	Cash which is property of the city must be kept separate from private or unofficial monies and must never be used for private or unofficial purposes. City safes should not be used to hold personal items or unofficial monies. (14)	Every employee involved in the handling of cash is responsible for its correctness and safe custody. Until the employee hands over the money in an authorized manner, he will be held responsible for any loss or deficiency or failure to account for such cash. (Ord. No. 2000-65, 9-7-2000)
Sec. 2-658. - Receipt, deposit and reconciliation of cash collected. (a)	Cash received in person. (1)	A receipt or validated water bill stub must be issued for each payment received. At a minimum, manual prenumbered receipts must include the date, mode of payment (cash, check or credit card) and the identification of the department and the person issuing the receipt. Machine generated receipts must contain similar information. (2)	All voided transactions are to be approved and initialed by the cash collection point supervisor. (3)	Only one cashier should be allowed to access a cash drawer during a single shift.(4)	Cash must be stored in a safe place until such cash is deposited.(b)	Cash received through the mail or drop box. (1)	An authorized employee must open the mail. Drop box receipts, which sometimes contain currency as well as cash, must be opened by two authorized employees. (2)	The checks should be entered into an approved accounts receivable system, if available, or if such system is not available, then a listing of the checks should be prepared or the checks should be photocopied and the copies retained as supporting documentation. The total of the checks should be utilized for reconciliation purposes. (3)	Cash must be stored in a safe place until such cash is deposited.(c)	Balancing of cash receipts. (1)	All cash received must be balanced daily by comparing the total of the cash, checks, credit card receipts, etc., to the cash register totals, the prenumbered receipt totals and the total of the money received by mail. (2)	Over/short amounts must be recorded separately, and investigated and resolved to the extent possible. (d)	Preparation of deposits. (1)	The preparation of deposits shall include counting the cash collection, verifying the check total and preparation of the deposit. (2)	The deposit must be prepared by a person not involved with collecting the cash or opening the mail. Under extraordinary circumstances, the finance director may authorize the revenue administrator to open payments received in the mail as well as complete the deposit. Such extraordinary circumstances include, but are not limited to, unusually high mail volume or inadequate staff to process the mail receipts due to vacation, illness or position vacancy. (3)	The cash receipts must be deposited by fund or location number using the appropriate deposit slip. (4)	The deposit must be taken directly to the bank by an authorized employee or handed over to an authorized guard in a bank-provided armored car. The armored car guard is to be given the deposit in a sealed bank bag and a grand total of the deposit. (e)	Reconciliation of cash collected. (1)	The reconciliation of cash collected must be performed by an employee who has no cash handling responsibilities. (2)	Monthly validated deposit slips must be reconciled to the receipts on the bank statements.(Ord. No. 2000-65, 9-7-2000)
Secs. 2-659—2-680. - Reserved. 
DIVISION 7. - PURCHASING CARD POLICY AND PROCEDURES 
Subdivision I. - Procuring Goods and/or Services Using a Purchasing Card 
Sec. 2-681. - Purpose. (a)	To establish policies and procedures for procuring goods and/or services using a purchasing card. Purchasing cards are referred to throughout this policy as the "P-Card." The purchasing card program is designed to streamline the purchasing and accounts payable process by reducing the paperwork generated by small dollar, high volume transactions, eliminating the need for purchase orders and facilitating quick payment to vendors. (b)	This policy includes procedures for the following:·	Establishing purchasing limits;·	Establishing allowable/prohibited purchases;·	Security;·	Charge transaction declines;·	Merchandise returns;·	Report processing;·	Reconciliation;·	Payment processing;·	Records management.(Ord. No. 2015-21, 9-24-2015)
Sec. 2-682. - Scope.     This policy applies to all City of Valdosta employees and elected officials. All purchasing cards shall be governed by this policy and used in a manner that complies with state law and city policy. (Ord. No. 2015-21, 9-24-2015)
Sec. 2-683. - Policy.     Employees who use the purchasing card to perform official city business will use the purchasing card as provided in this policy. (Ord. No. 2015-21, 9-24-2015)
Sec. 2-684. - Definitions.     [Terms are defined as follows:] (1)	Purchasing card - (also referred to herein as "P-Card"). The P-Card is a commercial credit card for small dollar purchases of goods and/or services necessary for official city business. The P-Card may be permanently issued to a named individual employee or elected official, a department or division, or temporarily issued to an employee traveling on city business. (2)	Purchasing card program administrator. The designee who will serve as a single point of contact between the city and the P-Card provider for general oversight of the purchasing card program. (3)	Departmental purchasing card coordinator. An individual or backup designated by the department head who is responsible for administration and control of the departmental implementation of the purchasing card policies and procedures. (4)	Purchasing cardholders. Full-time, permanent employees that have been designated by the department head to be issued a P-Card in their name for use under these policies and procedures. (5)	P-Card provider. The financial institution selected by the city to provide the P-Card program. (6)	Cut-off date. The monthly cut-off date is the last day of the P-Card provider's billing cycle. (Ord. No. 2015-21, 9-24-2015)
Sec. 2-685. - Responsibilities. (a)	It shall be the responsibility of the finance department to:(1)	Develop policy and procedures for the use of P-Cards that comply with state law.(2)	Administer the P-Card program, to include the following responsibilities:a.	Serve as primary contact with the P-Card provider for P-Cards.b.	Serve as primary contact with the departmental P-Card coordinators.c.	Approve/process applications for the issuance of P-Cards for users in compliance with the requirements as stated in the policy. d.	Establish guidelines and criteria for transactions and cumulative dollar limits for P-Cards. Cardholder limits will include monthly spending limits, individual transaction limits, and merchant category restrictions. These limits will be based on the cardholder's purchasing requirements and will not exceed the limits established by P-Card program administrator. e.	Approve/process changes to cardholder limits and restrictions as authorized by the city manager and department heads. f.	Maintain a current list of cardholders, card numbers and card limits.g.	Coordinate training on P-Card usage and small purchase policies and procedures.h.	Review departmental compliance/submission of approved expense reports with receipt reconciliations. i.	Cancel and suspend cards as requested by the city manager, department heads or departmental P-Card coordinators. j.	Conduct monthly reviews of all purchasing card transactions. The review is designed to ensure compliance, identify noncompliance issues and misuse, and through corrective measures assist the city with improving compliance. The monthly review and audit should happen within 15 days of the start of a new P-Card cycle. After completing the audit the administrator shall notify cardholders of any violations or questions the administrator has that occurred within the previous P-Card cycle. Depending on the severity of the violation, the administrator may suspend or revoke the use of the purchasing card. k.	Coordinate any system updates needed to interface with the city's accounting system. Review transactions for verification of small dollar purchases and price agreement opportunities. l.	Process general ledger interface for monthly county P-Card purchases.(3)	Provide direction for vendor enrollment.(4)	Establish general ledger hierarchy for P-Card purchases in conjunction with information technology department. (5)	Review expense reports and monthly billing statement from the P-Card provider and ensure timely payments of indebtedness. (6)	Review or perform necessary accounting transactions to process all departmental charges and ensure reconciliation account zeros out monthly. (7)	Conduct random audits of P-Card transactions to act as a check on departments carrying out their responsibility for audit and compliance with state law and city policies 5.3. It shall be the responsibility of all department heads to: (8)	Designate which employees will receive a P-Card.(9)	Recommend suspension or cancellation of a card to P-Card program administrator.(b)	Notify P-Card program administrator to cancel card privileges, if employee is terminated or changes positions; collection of card from employees. (1)	Designate departmental P-Card coordinator (and alternate) for each department who will be responsible for the following: a.	Verify that information on requests for purchasing cards is correct and that P-Cards are issued within the guidelines established by P-Card program administrator. b.	Monitor purchases made by cardholders.c.	Enforce timely compliance of submission requirements; review receipt sand expense report reconciliation for submission to the P-Card program administrator. Maintain all necessary documentation to support all purchases made by P-Card. d.	Code general ledger account numbers to online card transactions before the deadline established by the P-Card administrator. e.	Review P-Card applications or changes to card controls prior to submission.f.	Designate a system to maintain receipts and reconcile to expense report for each cardholder reporting to him/her. (2)	Designated cardholders will be responsible for the following:a.	Read and sign a purchasing card cardholder agreement prior to being issued a P-Card.b.	Assume responsibility for all purchases made with the P-Card, adhering to this policy insuring that no unauthorized purchases are made. Unauthorized purchases could be considered misappropriation of city funds. c.	Inform merchant of tax exempt status.d.	Provide receipts to the departmental P-Card coordinator on a daily basis.e.	Immediately report lost or stolen cards to the P-Card provider toll-free number and the P-Card program administrator by phone and then notify the department P-Card coordinator. f.	Make every reasonable effort to resolve disputed purchases with the vendor.g.	Immediately report all unresolved disputed purchases to the departmental P-Card coordinator.(Ord. No. 2015-21, 9-24-2015)
Sec. 2-686. - Procedures. (a)	Purchasing limits. The finance department will establish monthly and transaction limits for individual P-Cards. (b)	Purchases allowed with the purchasing card. Purchasing cards may not be used to purchase any item and/or service for immediate use not prohibited by law, this policy, or other policies approved by the mayor and council. The total purchase with the P-Card will not exceed the limits established for that card. All other purchasing policies remain in effect and P-Cards should not be used to circumvent them. (c)	Purchases prohibited with the purchasing card: (1)	Personal expenditures.(2)	Cash advances or refunds.(3)	The purchase of alcoholic beverages.(4)	Separate, sequential, and component purchases or transactions made with the intent to circumvent state law or city policy. (5)	Purchases that are split to stay within card transaction limits.(6)	Transaction amounts greater than cardholder's transaction limit.(7)	Other purchases specifically excluded in other city policies or by law.(d)	Security. The cardholder is responsible for the security of the card. This card should be treated with the same level of care as the cardholder would use with his/her own personal charge cards. (e)	Supporting documentation for card purchases. All transactions must be supported by receipts or credit slips. In instances where the receipt is lost, cardholder must obtain a copy at their own expense from the vendor or P-Card provider. For purchases made over the phone or on the internet, a logging system with unique transaction identifies should be maintained and a faxed copy or e-mail confirmation of the order retained as the receipt. (f)	Declined transactions. (1)	If a vendor receives a "decline" response from the P-Card provider after attempting to put through a P-Card transaction, cardholders should contact the P-Card program administrator with the following information for resolution: a.	Account number;b.	Business where decline occurred;c.	Total transaction amount of the decline;d.	Date the decline occurred.(2)	After determining the reason for the "decline" it may be necessary for the P-Card program administrator to contact the P-Card program coordinator for temporary or permanent changes to the cardholder's control limits to process the transaction. (g)	Using the card. In making a purchase, the cardholder must abide by the following rules: (1)	The cardholder must ensure that the item or service purchased is not restricted under subsection (c) of this section. (2)	In purchasing an item or service the cardholder must ensure that sales tax is not included in the purchase price before issuing payment with the P-Card. (3)	The cardholder must retain the purchase receipt and submit it to the P-Card program administrator. (h)	Purchasing return. The cardholder is responsible for obtaining a credit memo from the vendor when merchandise purchased with the card is later returned to the vendor for any reason. The credit memo will be attached to the expense report along with the sales receipt. (i)	Reconciliation of card purchases. (1)	The departmental P-Card coordinator is responsible for ensuring that all purchase receipts are collected and reconciled to transactions charged to their department. (2)	All transactions must be coded in the P-Card provider's system by the deadline set by the P-Card administrator. (j)	Records management. The departmental P-Card program coordinators must maintain all original receipts in a secure location in accordance with the city's record retention policy. (k)	Lost or stolen purchasing cards. When it is determined that P-Card has been lost or stolen, it is imperative to first cancel the card with the P-Card provider by calling the P-Card provider's toll-free number. In addition, the cardholder must also notify the P-Card program administrator of the loss by phone. Once a P-Card is discovered lost or stolen, it is imperative to cancel the card immediately. (l)	Changes to existing accounts. To make changes to an existing P-Card account, a department head should email the requested change to the finance director and the P-Card program administrator. (m)	Unauthorized use of the purchasing card. (1)	Any purchases that the P-Card program administrator deems prohibited as defined in subsection (c), will be sent back to the cardholder for justification and/or explanation. If any prohibited charges appear in the cardholder's transactions, the following may occur: a.	The P-Card program administrator will investigate all circumstances surrounding alleged misuse of the P-Card and in cases where there is evidence of a procedure or policy violation; refer that information to the appropriate authority for investigations and/or disciplinary action. b.	Termination of employment and forfeiture of the P-Card are potential disciplinary actions for improper use of the card. c.	In those cases where there is evidence of negligent use of the P-Card, but no fraudulent acts have been committed, the cardholder will be required to surrender the P-Card with all further privileges revoked. (2)	Any employee having knowledge of violations to this procedure or any other procedure or policy governing the use of the P-Card must immediately report such activity to the P-Card program administrator. (3)	The P-Card may be suspended or terminated if a purchasing cardholder is suspected of fraud, theft or illegal drug use. Should the suspicion prove founded, appropriate action shall be taken in accordance with existing city policies and procedures. (n)	Disputed items. Disputes, if possible, should be resolved promptly between the cardholder and the vendor. Cardholders should raise disputes immediately. As failure to do so will result in an authorized purchase that the department is responsible for paying even though the charge is incorrect. If the dispute cannot be resolved, the cardholder should notify the P-Card program administrator. A charge should not be disputed in the current P-Card cycle if it was returned for credit after the cut-off date. The credit should be coded to the original charge's account. (o)	Termination clause. (1)	The P-Card is issued to an employee for the city's convenience and may be suspended or terminated at any time by the city for noncompliance with city policies and procedures. Transfer, resignation or terminations of employment are grounds for cancellation of the P-Card. The department head or P-Card program coordinator should notify the P-Card program administrator. (2)	It is important to cancel a card immediately upon an employee's separation from employment.(Ord. No. 2015-21, 9-24-2015)
Secs. 2-687—2-700. - Reserved. 
Subdivision II. - Purchasing Card (P-Card) Policy for Elected Officials[14] Footnotes: --- (14) --- Editor's note—Ord. No. 2015-20, § 1, adopted Sept. 24, 2015, set out provisions intended for use as § 2-52. For purposes of classification and clarity, and at the editor's discretion, these provisions have been included as §§ 2-701—2-710.
Sec. 2-701. - Overview.     The Georgia General Assembly established guidelines and penalties into the Official Code of Georgia, Annotated ("O.C.G.A.") which provides that no municipal corporation shall issue governmental purchasing cards or government credit cards to elected officials on or after January 1, 2016, until the governing authority of the municipal corporation, by public vote, has authorized the issuance and has promulgated specific policies regarding the use of such government purchasing cards or government credit cards for elected officials of such municipal corporation. (Ord. No. 2015-20, § 1, 9-24-2015)
Sec. 2-702. - Purpose.     The purpose of this policy is to set requirements and standards for the City of Valdosta Purchasing Card Program. The policy is not intended to replace current State of Georgia Statutes, but is intended to comply with such state laws and establish more efficient guidelines for elected officials using such purchasing cards. At no time should a city-issued purchasing card be used for personal purchases regardless of circumstances. Utilizing the purchasing card or credit card for personal use or for any item or service not directly related to such official's public duty may result in disciplinary action including, but not limited to, felony criminal prosecution. All purchases utilizing a City of Valdosta purchasing card must be in accordance with these guidelines and with state law. (Ord. No. 2015-20, § 1, 9-24-2015)
Sec. 2-703. - Scope.     This purchasing card policy, as required by state law under O.C.G.A. § 36-80-24(c), applies to the use of City of Valdosta purchasing cards by elected officials authorized to be issued such purchasing cards. The Mayor and Council of the City of Valdosta have been authorized by the governing authority of the city to use purchasing cards and must abide by all of the applicable state laws and this purchasing card policy. (Ord. No. 2015-20, § 1, 9-24-2015)
Sec. 2-704. - Public inspection.     In accordance with O.C.G.A. § 36-80-24(b), any documents related to purchases using government purchasing cards or government credit cards incurred by elected officials shall be available for public inspection. (Ord. No. 2015-20, § 1, 9-24-2015)
Sec. 2-705. - Transaction limits.     Transaction limits are hereby established to insure compliance with state purchasing laws, maintain proper budgetary controls, and to minimize excessive use of any individual credit line. Individual monthly card limits cannot exceed those established by the mayor and council. The established single transaction limit for each card issued to an elected official must be no more than $6,000.00 in the case of the mayor or $3,000.00 in all other cases. The established monthly card limit is based upon the city's budgetary constraints and is no more than $12,000.00 per month for a card issued to the mayor and $6,000.00 for cards issued to other elected officials. Any exceptions to the standardized limits must have express written approval by the mayor and council and must be added to this policy by amendment or addendum. (Ord. No. 2015-20, § 1, 9-24-2015)
Sec. 2-706. - Purchasing restrictions. (a)	Elected officials may not use a government purchasing card or government credit card for the following: (1)	Any purchases of items for personal use.(2)	Cash refunds or advances.(3)	Any transaction amount greater than the transaction limits set forth by this policy.(4)	Items specifically restricted by this policy, unless a special exemption is granted by the municipal governing authority. (5)	Alcohol or liquor of any kind. Such purchases should not be made with the purchasing card and may not be reimbursed by the city. (6)	Purchases or transactions made with the intent to circumvent the city purchasing policy, transaction limits or state law. (b)	Elected officials may use government purchasing cards or government credit cards to purchase goods and/or services not prohibited by this policy or state law. Such purchases include, but are not limited to: (1)	Purchases of items for official city use which fall within the transactional restrictions of this policy. (2)	Purchasing of lodging, fuel, food, non-alcoholic beverages, or education and training materials while on city business. (3)	Emergency purchases necessary to protect city property.(Ord. No. 2015-20, § 1, 9-24-2015)
Sec. 2-707. - Administrator.     The city designates the office of finance director, as the program administrator of government purchasing cards or government credit cards. Such administrator shall: (1)	Serve as a liaison between the city's cardholders and the issuers of such cards.(2)	Maintain the cardholder agreement for all cardholders.(3)	Provide instruction, training and assistance to cardholders.(4)	Maintain account information and secure all cardholder information.(5)	Keep cardholders up-to-date on new or changing information.(6)	Upon receipt of information indicating fraudulent use or lost/stolen cards, immediately report it to appropriate parties, including the issuer. (7)	Ensure all card accounts are being utilized properly as set forth by state law and this policy. (8)	Define the city's policy and procedures for proper documentation and storage of receipts, logs and approvals required under this policy. (9)	Identify any changes to named persons authorized to use a government purchasing card or government credit card. (10)	Any other duties assigned by the municipal governing authority.(Ord. No. 2015-20, § 1, 9-24-2015)
Sec. 2-708. - Accounting and auditing.     The administrator, in an effort to ensure compliance with city policy and state law, will conduct periodic reviews in accordance with city's general P-Card policy. If a violation of policy is discovered, the administrator may suspend or revoke the use of the P-Card after notification to the cardholder and to the mayor and council, but only after consultation with the city attorney. Any unresolved violations should be reported to the mayor and council and the city attorney in writing within five business days. (Ord. No. 2015-20, § 1, 9-24-2015)
Sec. 2-709. - Violations.     The use of a government purchasing card or government credit card may be suspended or revoked when the administrator, after consultation with the city attorney, determines that the cardholder has violated the approved policies or state law regarding the use of a government purchasing card or government credit card. The government purchasing card or government credit card shall be revoked whenever a cardholder is removed from office with the city and shall be suspended if such elected official has been suspended from the office. (Ord. No. 2015-20, § 1, 9-24-2015)
Sec. 2-710. - Agreement.     Before being issued a government purchasing card or government credit card under this policy and state law, all authorized users of government purchasing cards or government credit cards shall sign and accept below indicating that such user will use such cards only in accordance with the policies of the city and with the requirements of state law. (Ord. No. 2015-20, § 1, 9-24-2015)
Secs. 2-711—2-730. - Reserved. 
Chapter 4 - ADULT ESTABLISHMENTS[1] Footnotes: --- (1) --- Cross reference— Alcoholic beverages, ch. 6; business regulations, ch. 22; zoning, app. A.State Law reference— State licensing of coin-operated amusement machines, O.C.G.A. § 48-17-1 et seq.
ARTICLE I. - IN GENERAL 
Sec. 4-1. - Purpose.     The purpose of this chapter is to regulate certain types of businesses, including, but not limited to, adult entertainment establishments, to the end that the many types of criminal activities frequently engendered by such businesses will be curtailed. Other communities and cities, including Marietta, Georgia, Fulton County, Georgia and Savannah, Georgia, have recognized that regulation of adult entertainment establishments helps to end or curtail many types of criminal activity. However, it is recognized that such regulation cannot de facto approach prohibition; otherwise, a protected form of expression would vanish. As to adult dance establishments, this chapter represents a balancing of competing interests: Reduced criminal activity and protection of the neighborhoods through the regulation of adult entertainment establishments versus the protected rights of adult entertainment establishments and patrons. (Ord. No. 2006-57, § 1, 9-21-2006)
Sec. 4-2. - Definitions.     The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning:     Adult bookstore means an establishment having a substantial or significant portion of its stock in trade, books, magazines or other periodicals which are distinguished or characterized by their emphasis on matter depicting, describing or relating to specified sexual activities or specified anatomical areas, or an establishment with a segment or section comprising 20 percent of its net sales consisting of printed material which are distinguished or characterized by their emphasis on matter depicting, describing or relating to specified sexual activities or specified anatomical areas.     Adult business means either: (1)	Any business other than those expressly specified in this chapter, where employees or patrons expose specified anatomical areas or engage in specified sexual activities; or (2)	Any other business or establishment which offers its patrons services or entertainment characterized by an emphasis on matter depicting, describing, discussing, or relating to specified sexual activities or specified anatomical areas.     Adult dancing establishment means a business that features dancers displaying or exposing specified anatomical areas.     Adult hotel or motel means a hotel or motel wherein material is presented which is distinguished or characterized by an emphasis on matter depicting, describing, or relating to specified sexual activities or specified anatomical areas.     Adult minimotion picture theater means an enclosed building with a capacity for less than 50 persons used for presenting material distinguished or characterized by an emphasis on matter depicting or relating to specified sexual activities or specified anatomical areas for observation by patrons therein.     Adult motion picture arcade means any place to which the public is permitted or invited wherein coin- or slug-operated, or electronically, electrically or mechanically controlled, still or motion picture machines, projectors or other image-producing devices are maintained to show images to five or fewer persons per machine at any one time and where the images so displayed are distinguished or characterized by an emphasis on depicting or describing specified sexual activities or specified anatomical areas.     Adult motion picture theater means an enclosed building with a capacity of 50 or more persons, used for presenting material distinguished or characterized by an emphasis on matter depicting, describing or relating to specified sexual activities or specified anatomical areas for observation by patrons therein.     Adult video store means any establishment having a substantial or significant portion of its stock in trade, video tapes or movies or other reproductions, whether for sale or rent, which are distinguished or characterized by their emphasis on matter depicting, describing or relating to specified sexual activities or specified anatomical areas or an establishment with a segment or section, comprising five percent of its total floor space, devoted to the sale or display of such material or which derives more than five percent its net sales from videos which are characterized or distinguished or relating to specified sexual activities or specified anatomical areas.     Church means a temple or building consecrated to the honor of God or other supreme being and religion; or an assembly of persons united by the profession of the same religious faith, meeting together routinely for religious worship.     Encounter center or rap establishment means any business, agency or person who, for any form of consideration or gratuity, provides a place where two or more persons may congregate, assemble or associate for the primary purpose of engaging in, describing or discussing specified sexual activities, or exposing specified anatomical areas.     Erotic dance establishment means a nightclub, theater or other establishment which features live performances by topless and/or bottomless dancers, go-go dancers, strippers or similar entertainers, where such performances are distinguished or characterized by an emphasis on specified sexual activities or specified anatomical areas.     Escort bureau or introduction services means any business, agency or person who, for a fee, commission, hire, reward or profit, furnishes or offers to furnish names or persons, or who introduces, furnishes or arranges for persons who may accompany other persons to or about social affairs, entertainments or places of amusement, or who may consort with others about any place of public resort or within any private quarters.     Good moral character means a person is of good moral character according to this chapter if that person has not been convicted of a drug-related or alcohol-related felony or sex-related crime in the past five years.     Minor means any person who has not attained the age of 18 years.     Specified anatomical areas means and includes any of the following: (1)	Less than completely and opaquely covered human genitals or pubic region, buttock, or female breast below a point immediately above the top of the areola; or (2)	Human male genitalia in a discernibly turgid state, even if completely and opaquely covered.     Specified sexual activities means and includes any of the following: (1)	Actual or simulated sexual intercourse, oral copulation, anal intercourse, oral anal copulation, bestiality, direct physical stimulation of unclothed genitals, flagellation or torture in the context of a sexual relationship, or the use of excretory functions in the context of a sexual relations, and any of the following sexually oriented acts or conduct: anilingus, buggery, coprophagy, coprophilia, cunnilingus, fellatio, necrophilia, pederasty, pedophilia, piquerism, sapphism, zooerasty; (2)	Clearly depicted human genitals in a state of sexual stimulation, arousal or tumescence;(3)	Use of human or animal ejaculation, sodomy, oral copulation, coitus, or masturbation;(4)	Fondling or touching of nude human genitals, pubic region, buttocks or female breast;(5)	Masochism, erotic or sexually oriented torture, beating or the inflicting of pain;(6)	Erotic or lewd touching, fondling or other sexual contact with an animal by a human being; or (7)	Human excretion, urination, menstruation, vaginal or anal irrigation.(Ord. No. 2006-57, § 2, 9-21-2006)
Sec. 4-3. - Regulations. (a)	No person shall advertise, or cause to be advertised, an adult entertainment establishment, as defined in section 4-2, without a valid adult entertainment occupation tax certificate issued pursuant to this chapter. (b)	No later than March 1 of each year, an adult entertainment establishment applicant shall file a verified report with the license officer showing the applicant's gross receipts and amounts paid to dancers for the preceding calendar year. (c)	An adult entertainment establishment applicant shall maintain and retain for a period of two years the names, addresses, and ages of all persons employed as dancers. (d)	No adult entertainment establishment applicant shall employ or contract with as a dancer a person under the age of 18 years or a person not licensed pursuant to this chapter. (e)	No person under the age of 18 years shall be admitted to an adult entertainment establishment.(f)	An adult entertainment establishment, as defined in section 4-2, shall be closed between 2:00 a.m. and 9:00 a.m. on weekdays and 2:55 a.m. and 9:00 a.m. on Saturday and Sunday. (g)	No dancer shall fondle or caress any patron and no patron shall fondle or caress any dancer. (h)	If any portion, or subsection, of this section, or its application to any person or circumstance, is held invalid by a court of competent jurisdiction, the remainder of application to other persons or circumstances shall not be affected. (Ord. No. 2006-57, § 3, 9-21-2006)
Sec. 4-4. - Certain activities prohibited.     No person shall publicly display or expose or suffer the public display or exposure, with less than a full opaque covering, of any portion or a person's genitals, pubic area or buttocks in a lewd and obscene fashion. (Ord. No. 2006-57, § 4, 9-21-2006)
